A wife is bound by law for as long as her husband lives. But if her husband dies, she is free to marry whom she wishes, only in the Lord.

(1 Corinthians 7:40) 
But in my judgment, she is happier if she remains as she is. And I think that I also have the Spirit of God.

(1 Corinthians 8:1) 
Now about the things that have been sacrificed to idols: we know that we all have knowledge. Knowledge by itself causes pride, but charity builds up the Church.

(1 Corinthians 8:2) 
If anyone thinks he knows something, he doesn’t yet know it the way he should.

(1 Corinthians 8:3) 
But if anyone loves God, he is known by Him.

(1 Corinthians 8:4) 
Concerning the eating of food offered to idols, we know that an idol is nothing in the world, and that there is no God except for the One God.

(1 Corinthians 8:5) 
Even if there are those who are called gods, whether in the sky or on the earth, as there are many gods and many lords:

(1 Corinthians 8:6) 
For us, there is only one God the Father, from whom all things come and in whom we live; and one Lord Jesus Christ, through whom all things are, and through whom we live.

(1 Corinthians 8:7) 
But not everyone has this knowledge. Some, through their attachment to idols, eat food that has been sacrificed to idols, and because their conscience is weak, they are defiled.

(1 Corinthians 8:8) 
Food does not recommend us to God. For if we eat, we are not better; and if we do not eat, we are not worse off.

(1 Corinthians 8:9) 
But be careful that your freedom of conscience does not become an occasion of stumbling for the weak.

(1 Corinthians 8:10) 
For if someone sees you who has knowledge eating in an idol’s temple, won’t the conscience of the weak man be emboldened to eat food sacrificed to idols?

(1 Corinthians 8:11) 
So by your knowledge, the weak brother will be destroyed, because Christ died for him.

(1 Corinthians 8:12) 
When you sin against your brothers and wound their weak conscience, you sin against Christ.

(1 Corinthians 8:13) 
Therefore, if food causes my brother to stumble, I will never eat meat again, lest I cause my brother to stumble.

(1 Corinthians 9:1) 
Am I not an Apostle? Am I not free? Have I not seen Jesus Christ Our Lord? Are you not the fruit of my ministry in the Lord?

(1 Corinthians 9:2) 
Even if I am not an Apostle to others, I am certainly one to you. You are proof that I am an Apostle of the Lord.

(1 Corinthians 9:3) 
To those who question me, this is my defense:

(1 Corinthians 9:4) 
Do we not have the right to eat and drink?

(1 Corinthians 9:5) 
Do we not have the right to take a wife, a sister in the faith, as do the other Apostles, and the brothers of the Lord, and Cephas?

(1 Corinthians 9:6) 
Or is it only Barnabas and I who do not have the right to stop working to support ourselves?

(1 Corinthians 9:7) 
Who serves as a soldier at his own expense? Who plants a vineyard and does not eat of its fruit? Or who tends a flock and does not eat of the milk of the flock?

(1 Corinthians 9:8) 
Am I speaking merely as a man? Does not the Law also speak these things?

(1 Corinthians 9:9) 
For it is written in the Law of Moses, “You shall not muzzle the ox that treads out the grain.” Is it for oxen that God is concerned?

(1 Corinthians 9:10) 
Or does He speak entirely for our sake? Indeed, it was written for our sake, so that he who plows should plow in hope, and he who threshes should thresh in hope of receiving a share of the harvest.

(1 Corinthians 9:11) 
If we have sown spiritual things for you, is it a great thing if we reap your material things?

(1 Corinthians 9:12) 
If others share in your rights, why not even more so we? But we have not used this right. We endure anything rather than put an obstacle in the way of the gospel of Christ.

(1 Corinthians 9:13) 
Do you not know that those who are employed in the temple service get their food from the temple, and those who serve at the altar share in the offerings?

(1 Corinthians 9:14) 
In the same way, the Lord commanded that those who proclaim the gospel should live by the gospel.

(1 Corinthians 9:15) 
But I have not used any of these rights, nor am I writing this in order that it may be done for me. For I would rather die than have anyone deprive me of my reason for boasting.

(1 Corinthians 9:16) 
For if I preach the gospel, I have no reason to boast, because an obligation is laid on me. Woe to me if I do not preach the gospel!

(1 Corinthians 9:17) 
For if I do this of my own will, I have a reward, but if I do it unwillingly, I am entrusted with a commission.

(1 Corinthians 9:18) 
What then is my reward? That, in preaching the gospel, I may offer the gospel free of charge, so as not to make full use of my right in the gospel.

(1 Corinthians 9:19) 
For though I am free from all, I have made myself a servant to all, that I might win more of them.

(1 Corinthians 9:20) 
To the Jews I became as a Jew, that I might win Jews. To those under the law I became as one under the law (though not being myself under the law) that I might win those under the law.

(1 Corinthians 9:21) 
To those outside the law I became as one outside the law (not being without the law of God but under the law of Christ), that I might win those outside the law.

(1 Corinthians 9:22) 
To the weak I became weak, that I might win the weak. I have become all things to all men, that I might by all means save some.

(1 Corinthians 9:23) 
I do it all for the sake of the gospel, that I may share with it.

(1 Corinthians 9:24) 
Do you not know that in a race all the runners run, but only one receives the prize? So run that you may obtain it.

(1 Corinthians 9:25) 
Every athlete exercises self-control in all things. They do it to receive a perishable wreath, but we an imperishable.

(1 Corinthians 9:26) 
So I do not run aimlessly; I do not box as one beating the air.

(1 Corinthians 9:27) 
But I discipline my body and keep it under control, lest after preaching to others I myself should be disqualified.

(1 Corinthians 10:1) 
And so, my brothers, I do not want you to be unaware that all our fathers were under the protection of the cloud, and all crossed through the sea,

(1 Corinthians 10:2) 
and all were baptized into Moses in the cloud and in the sea:

(1 Corinthians 10:3) 
and all ate the same spiritual food,

(1 Corinthians 10:4) 
and all drank the same spiritual drink. They drank from the spiritual rock that followed them, and that rock was Christ.

(1 Corinthians 10:5) 
But in many of them, God was not pleased; for they were struck down in the desert.

(1 Corinthians 10:6) 
These things happened as examples for us, so that we would not be eager for evil things, as they desired them.

(1 Corinthians 10:7) 
Do not become idolaters, as some of them did, as it is written: “The people sat down to eat and drink, and they rose up to play.”

(1 Corinthians 10:8) 
Nor should we engage in sexual immorality, as some of them did, and twenty-three thousand fell in one day.

(1 Corinthians 10:9) 
Nor let us tempt Christ, as some of them tempted, and perished by serpents.

(1 Corinthians 10:10) 
Nor should you grumble, as some of them grumbled, and perished by the destroyer.

(1 Corinthians 10:11) 
These things happened to them as examples, and they were written for our correction, upon whom the ends of the ages have come.

(1 Corinthians 10:12) 
Therefore, let whoever thinks he stands, take heed that he does not fall.

(1 Corinthians 10:13) 
No temptation has overtaken you that is not common to man. But God is faithful, who will not let you be tempted beyond what you can bear, but with the temptation will also make a way out, that you may be able to endure it.

(1 Corinthians 10:14) 
Therefore, my beloved ones, flee from idolatry.

(1 Corinthians 10:15) 
I speak as to the wise: judge for yourselves what I say.

(1 Corinthians 10:16) 
The cup of blessing which we bless, is it not the communion of the blood of Christ? The bread which we break, is it not the participation of the body of Christ?

(1 Corinthians 10:17) 
Because there is one bread, we who are many are one body, for we all partake of the one bread.

(1 Corinthians 10:18) 
Consider Israel according to the flesh: are not those who eat of the sacrifices partakers of the altar?

(1 Corinthians 10:19) 
What do I say then? That an idol is anything, or that which is sacrificed to idols is anything?

(1 Corinthians 10:20) 
No, but that the things which the Gentiles sacrifice they sacrifice to demons and not to God. I do not want you to become partners with demons.

(1 Corinthians 10:21) 
You cannot drink the cup of the Lord and the cup of demons; you cannot partake of the table of the Lord and the table of demons.

(1 Corinthians 10:22) 
Or do we provoke the Lord to jealousy? Are we stronger than He?

(1 Corinthians 10:23) 
“All things are lawful,” but not all things are helpful. “All things are lawful,” but not all things edify.

(1 Corinthians 10:24) 
Let no one seek his own, but that of another.

(1 Corinthians 10:25) 
Eat anything that is sold in the meat market, asking no questions for conscience’ sake.

(1 Corinthians 10:26) 
“The earth is the Lord’s, and all its fullness.”

(1 Corinthians 10:27) 
If any of the unbelievers invites you, and you wish to go, eat whatever is set before you, asking no question for conscience’ sake.

(1 Corinthians 10:28) 
But if anyone says to you, “This was offered to idols,” do not eat it for the sake of the one who informed you, and for conscience’ sake.

(1 Corinthians 10:29) 
I mean conscience, not your own, but the other person’s; for why is my freedom judged by another’s conscience?

(1 Corinthians 10:30) 
If I partake with thanks, why am I blasphemed for that for which I give thanks?

(1 Corinthians 10:31) 
So then, whether you eat or drink, or whatever you do, do all to the glory of God.

(1 Corinthians 10:32) 
Give no offense to Jews or to Greeks or to the church of God,

(1 Corinthians 10:33) 
just as I also please all men in everything, not seeking my own profit, but the profit of many, that they may be saved.

(1 Corinthians 11:1) 
Imitate me, even as I imitate Christ.

(1 Corinthians 11:2) 
I commend you, brothers, for always remembering me and for keeping the teachings that I handed down to you.

(1 Corinthians 11:3) 
I want you to understand this: every man has Christ as his head, a woman has a man as her head, and Christ has God as His head.

(1 Corinthians 11:4) 
Any man who prays or prophesies with his head covered dishonors his head.

(1 Corinthians 11:5) 
And any woman who prays or prophesies with her head uncovered dishonors her head, because it is as though she had her head shaved.

(1 Corinthians 11:6) 
For if a woman does not cover her head, she should have her hair cut off. But if it is shameful for a woman to cut off her hair or shave her head, then she should cover it.

(1 Corinthians 11:7) 
A man, since he is the image and glory of God, shouldn't have his head covered. But woman is the glory of man.

(1 Corinthians 11:8) 
For man wasn't created from woman, but woman from man.

(1 Corinthians 11:9) 
Man wasn't created for the sake of woman, but woman for the sake of man.

(1 Corinthians 11:10) 
That is why a woman should have a sign of authority on her head, because of the angels.

(1 Corinthians 11:11) 
Nevertheless, neither is woman independent of man in the Lord, nor is man independent of woman.

(1 Corinthians 11:12) 
For just as woman came from man, so also man is born of woman. But all things are from God.

(1 Corinthians 11:13) 
Judge for yourselves: is it proper for a woman to pray to God with her head uncovered?

(1 Corinthians 11:14) 
Doesn't nature itself teach you that if a man has long hair, it is a dishonor to him,

(1 Corinthians 11:15) 
but if a woman has long hair, it is her glory? For her hair has been given to her for a covering.

(1 Corinthians 11:16) 
But if anyone seems to be contentious, we have no such practice, nor do the churches of God.

(1 Corinthians 11:17) 
But in the following instructions, I do not praise you, because you come together not for the better, but for the worse.

(1 Corinthians 11:18) 
For first of all, when you come together in church, I hear that there are divisions among you, and in part I believe it.

(1 Corinthians 11:19) 
For there must be factions among you, so that those who are approved may be evident among you.

(1 Corinthians 11:20) 
So then, when you meet together, it is not really to eat the Lord's Supper.

(1 Corinthians 11:21) 
For in eating, each one goes ahead with his own supper, and one person is hungry while another is drunk.

(1 Corinthians 11:22) 
Do you not have houses to eat and drink in? Or do you despise the church of God, and shame those who have nothing? What shall I say to you? Shall I praise you in this? I do not praise you.

(1 Corinthians 11:23) 
For I received from the Lord what I also handed down to you: that the Lord Jesus, on the night when He was betrayed, took bread,

(1 Corinthians 11:24) 
and when He had given thanks, He broke it, and said, “Take, eat; this is My body, which is broken for you; do this in remembrance of Me.”

(1 Corinthians 11:25) 
In the same way He also took the cup after supper, saying, “This cup is the new covenant in My blood; do this, as often as you drink it, in remembrance of Me.”

(1 Corinthians 11:26) 
For as often as you eat this bread and drink the cup, you proclaim the Lord’s death until He comes.

(1 Corinthians 11:27) 
Therefore whoever eats the bread or drinks the cup of the Lord in an unworthy manner, shall be guilty of the body and the blood of the Lord.

(1 Corinthians 11:28) 
But a man must examine himself, and so eat of the bread and drink of the cup.

(1 Corinthians 11:29) 
For anyone who eats and drinks without discerning the body, eats and drinks judgment on himself.

(1 Corinthians 11:30) 
For this reason many among you are weak and sick, and a number are dying.

(1 Corinthians 11:31) 
But if we judged ourselves rightly, we would not be judged.

(1 Corinthians 11:32) 
But when we are judged, we are disciplined by the Lord so that we will not be condemned with the world.

(1 Corinthians 11:33) 
So then, my brothers, when you come together to eat, wait for one another.

(1 Corinthians 11:34) 
If anyone is hungry, let him eat at home, so that you will not come together for judgment. And the remaining matters I will arrange when I come.

(1 Corinthians 12:1) 
Regarding spiritual gifts, brothers, I do not want you to be ignorant.

(1 Corinthians 12:2) 
You know that when you were Gentiles, you were being led astray, running to idols, which cannot speak, as you were led.

(1 Corinthians 12:3) 
Therefore, I make it known to you that no one speaking by the Spirit of God says: “Jesus is accursed.” And no one can say “Lord Jesus” except in the Holy Spirit.

(1 Corinthians 12:4) 
Now there are varieties of gifts, but the same Spirit.

(1 Corinthians 12:5) 
And there are varieties of ministries, and the same Lord.

(1 Corinthians 12:6) 
And there are varieties of workings, but it is the same God who works all things in all.

(1 Corinthians 12:7) 
To each one is given the manifestation of the Spirit for profit.

(1 Corinthians 12:8) 
For to one, through the Spirit, is given the word of wisdom; to another, the word of knowledge, according to the same Spirit:

(1 Corinthians 12:9) 
to another, faith in the same Spirit; to another, the grace of healings in the one Spirit:

(1 Corinthians 12:10) 
to another, the working of miracles; to another, prophecy; to another, the discernment of spirits; to another, various kinds of tongues; to another, interpretation of words.

(1 Corinthians 12:11) 
But all these things are worked by one and the same Spirit, distributing to each one individually as He wills.

(1 Corinthians 12:12) 
For as the body is one and has many members, but all the members of the body, though many, are one body, so also is Christ.

(1 Corinthians 12:13) 
For in one Spirit we were all baptized into one body, whether Jews or Gentiles, whether slaves or free; and we were all given to drink of one Spirit.

(1 Corinthians 12:14) 
For the body is not one member, but many.

(1 Corinthians 12:15) 
If the foot should say, “Because I am not a hand, I am not of the body,” it is not therefore not of the body?

(1 Corinthians 12:16) 
And if the ear should say, “Because I am not an eye, I am not of the body,” it is not therefore not of the body?

(1 Corinthians 12:17) 
If the whole body were an eye, where would the hearing be? If the whole were hearing, where would the smelling be?

(1 Corinthians 12:18) 
But now God has placed the members, each one of them, in the body, as He willed.

(1 Corinthians 12:19) 
If all were one member, where would the body be?

(1 Corinthians 12:20) 
Now indeed there are many members, but one body.

(1 Corinthians 12:21) 
The eye cannot say to the hand, “I have no need of you,” or again the head to the feet, “I have no need of you.”

(1 Corinthians 12:22) 
Rather, those members of the body which seem to be weaker are more necessary.

(1 Corinthians 12:23) 
And those members of the body that we think to be less honorable, these we surround with greater honor; and those parts that are unpresentable, we have the greater honor.

(1 Corinthians 12:24) 
But the parts that are honorable have no need. But God has tempered the body together, giving greater honor to the one which lacked honor,

(1 Corinthians 12:25) 
so that there would be no division in the body, but that the members would have the same care for one another.

(1 Corinthians 12:26) 
And if one member suffers, all the members suffer with it; or if one member is honored, all the members rejoice with it.

(1 Corinthians 12:27) 
Now you are the body of Christ, and members of His body.

(1 Corinthians 12:28) 
And God has appointed in the Church, first apostles, second prophets, third teachers; then miracles, then gifts of healings, helps, administrations, various kinds of tongues.

(1 Corinthians 12:29) 
Are all apostles? Are all prophets? Are all teachers? Do all work miracles?

(1 Corinthians 12:30) 
Do all have gifts of healings? Do all speak in tongues? Do all interpret?

(1 Corinthians 12:31) 
But earnestly desire the greater gifts. And I show you a still more excellent way.

(1 Corinthians 13:1) 
If I speak in the tongues of men, or even of angels, but do not have love, then I have become like a noisy gong, or a clanging cymbal.

(1 Corinthians 13:2) 
And if I have the gift of prophecy, and know all mysteries, and all knowledge, and if I have all faith, so as to move mountains, but do not have love, then I am nothing.

(1 Corinthians 13:3) 
And if I give away all my possessions to feed the poor, and if I deliver my body to be burned, but do not have love, it profits me nothing.

(1 Corinthians 13:4) 
Love endures with patience, and is kind. Love does not envy, does not parade itself, is not puffed up,

(1 Corinthians 13:5) 
is not ambitious, does not seek its own, is not provoked to anger, and does not think evil,

(1 Corinthians 13:6) 
does not rejoice in iniquity, but rejoices with the truth.

(1 Corinthians 13:7) 
It bears all things, believes all things, hopes all things, endures all things.

(1 Corinthians 13:8) 
Love never fails. But whether there are prophecies, they will be done away; whether there are tongues, they will cease; or whether there is knowledge, it will be destroyed.

(1 Corinthians 13:9) 
For we know in part, and we prophesy in part.

(1 Corinthians 13:10) 
But when that which is perfect comes, then that which is in part will be done away.

(1 Corinthians 13:11) 
When I was a child, I spoke as a child, I understood as a child, I thought as a child. But when I became a man, I put away childish things.

(1 Corinthians 13:12) 
For now we see through a glass in a dark manner, but then we will see face to face. Now I know in part; but then I will know as I also am known.

(1 Corinthians 13:13) 
And now these three remain: faith, hope, and love. But the greatest of these is love.

(1 Corinthians 14:1) 
Pursue love. Be eager for the gifts of the Spirit, especially the gift of prophecy.

(1 Corinthians 14:2) 
Anyone who speaks in a language that no one understands is speaking to God, not to people. No one understands him. He is speaking mysteries in the Spirit.

(1 Corinthians 14:3) 
But the one who prophesies speaks to people, to build them up, encourage them, and comfort them.

(1 Corinthians 14:4) 
Anyone who speaks in a language that no one understands builds up himself. But the one who prophesies builds up the Church of God.

(1 Corinthians 14:5) 
I wish all of you spoke in languages, but even more that you prophesied. The one who prophesies is greater than the one who speaks in languages, unless he interprets, so that the Church may be built up.

(1 Corinthians 14:6) 
Now, brothers and sisters, if I come to you speaking in languages, how will I help you unless I speak to you in a revelation, or in knowledge, or in prophecy, or in teaching?

(1 Corinthians 14:7) 
Even lifeless instruments, such as the flute or the harp, must give a clear sound if they are to be understood. How will anyone know what is being played?

(1 Corinthians 14:8) 
If the trumpet gives an unclear sound, who will prepare for battle?

(1 Corinthians 14:9) 
So it is with you. Unless you speak intelligible words with your tongue, how will anyone know what you are saying? You will be speaking into the air.

(1 Corinthians 14:10) 
There are perhaps many kinds of languages in the world, and none is without meaning.

(1 Corinthians 14:11) 
If I do not understand the meaning of the language, I will be a foreigner to the speaker, and the speaker a foreigner to me.

(1 Corinthians 14:12) 
So it is with you. Since you are eager for gifts of the Spirit, seek to abound in them for the building up of the Church.

(1 Corinthians 14:13) 
Therefore, anyone who speaks in a language should pray that he may interpret it.

(1 Corinthians 14:14) 
For if I pray in a language, my spirit prays, but my mind is unfruitful.

(1 Corinthians 14:15) 
So what shall I do? I will pray with my spirit, but I will also pray with my mind. I will sing with my spirit, but I will also sing with my mind.

(1 Corinthians 14:16) 
Otherwise, if you give thanks in the Spirit, how can the one who is present as an outsider say “Amen” to your thanksgiving, since he does not know what you are saying?

(1 Corinthians 14:17) 
For you may be giving thanks well enough, but the other person is not built up.

(1 Corinthians 14:18) 
I give thanks to God that I speak in languages more than all of you.

(1 Corinthians 14:19) 
But in the church, I would rather speak five words with my mind, in order to instruct others, than ten thousand words in a language.

(1 Corinthians 14:20) 
Brothers and sisters, do not be children in your understanding. Be infants in evil, but in your thinking be mature.

(1 Corinthians 14:21) 
In the Law it is written: “By people of strange tongues and by the lips of foreigners I will speak to this people, and even then they will not listen to me,” says the Lord.

(1 Corinthians 14:22) 
So languages are a sign, not for believers, but for unbelievers. Prophecy, however, is not for unbelievers but for believers.

(1 Corinthians 14:23) 
So if the whole Church comes together and all speak in languages, and some unbelievers or uninstructed people come in, will they not say that you are mad?

(1 Corinthians 14:24) 
But if all prophesy, and an unbeliever or uninstructed person comes in, he is convicted by all and is judged by all.

(1 Corinthians 14:25) 
And so the secrets of his heart are disclosed, and, falling on his face, he will worship God, proclaiming that God is really among you.

(1 Corinthians 14:26) 
What then, brothers and sisters? When you come together, each one has a psalm, has a teaching, has a revelation, has a language, has an interpretation. Let all things be done for building up.

(1 Corinthians 14:27) 
If anyone speaks in a language, let there be only two or at most three, and let them speak one at a time, and let someone interpret.

(1 Corinthians 14:28) 
But if there is no one to interpret, let the speaker keep silent in the church and speak to himself and to God.

(1 Corinthians 14:29) 
Let two or three prophets speak, and let the others weigh what is said.

(1 Corinthians 14:30) 
If anything is revealed to another sitting nearby, let the first one be silent.

(1 Corinthians 14:31) 
For you can all prophesy one by one, so that all may learn and all be encouraged.

(1 Corinthians 14:32) 
And the spirits of the prophets are subject to the prophets.

(1 Corinthians 14:33) 
For God is not a God of confusion but of peace. As in all the churches of the saints,

(1 Corinthians 14:34) 
let the women keep silent in the churches. For they are not permitted to speak, but should be in submission, as the Law says.

(1 Corinthians 14:35) 
If there is anything they desire to learn, let them ask their husbands at home. For it is shameful for a woman to speak in church.

(1 Corinthians 14:36) 
Did the word of God originate with you? Or has it come only to you?

(1 Corinthians 14:37) 
If anyone thinks that he is a prophet, or spiritual, let him recognize that the things which I am writing to you are the commandments of the Lord.

(1 Corinthians 14:38) 
If anyone does not recognize them, he will not be recognized.

(1 Corinthians 14:39) 
So, brothers and sisters, be eager to prophesy, and do not forbid speaking in languages.

(1 Corinthians 14:40) 
But all things should be done decently and in order.

(1 Corinthians 15:1) 
Brothers, I want you to know the Gospel that I preached to you, that you received, and in which you stand,

(1 Corinthians 15:2) 
by which you are saved, if you hold fast to the Gospel that I preached to you, unless you have believed in vain.

(1 Corinthians 15:3) 
For I delivered to you first of all what I also received: that Christ died for our sins according to the Scriptures,

(1 Corinthians 15:4) 
and that He was buried, and that He rose on the third day according to the Scriptures,

(1 Corinthians 15:5) 
and that He was seen by Cephas, and then by the eleven.

(1 Corinthians 15:6) 
After that, He was seen by more than five hundred brothers at once; most of whom are still alive, but some have fallen asleep.

(1 Corinthians 15:7) 
Then He was seen by James, and then by all the Apostles.

(1 Corinthians 15:8) 
And last of all, as to one untimely born, He was seen by me also.

(1 Corinthians 15:9) 
For I am the least of the Apostles, who am not worthy to be called an Apostle, because I persecuted the Church of God.

(1 Corinthians 15:10) 
But by the grace of God I am what I am, and His grace in me has not been in vain. On the contrary, I worked harder than any of them, though it was not I, but the grace of God with me.

(1 Corinthians 15:11) 
Whether it was I or they, so we preach and so you believed.

(1 Corinthians 15:12) 
Now if Christ is preached as having been raised from the dead, how do some among you say that there is no resurrection of the dead?

(1 Corinthians 15:13) 
For if there is no resurrection of the dead, then Christ has not been raised either.

(1 Corinthians 15:14) 
And if Christ has not been raised, then our preaching is in vain, and your faith is also in vain.

(1 Corinthians 15:15) 
We are even found to be false witnesses of God, because we testified against God that He raised Christ, whom He did not raise if the dead do not rise.

(1 Corinthians 15:16) 
For if the dead do not rise, then Christ has not been raised either.

(1 Corinthians 15:17) 
And if Christ has not been raised, your faith is vain; you are still in your sins.

(1 Corinthians 15:18) 
Then those who have fallen asleep in Christ have perished.

(1 Corinthians 15:19) 
If in this life only we have hoped in Christ, we are of all men most to be pitied.

(1 Corinthians 15:20) 
But now Christ has been raised from the dead, the firstfruits of those who have fallen asleep.

(1 Corinthians 15:21) 
For since by man came death, by man also came the resurrection of the dead.

(1 Corinthians 15:22) 
For as in Adam all die, so also in Christ shall all be made alive.

(1 Corinthians 15:23) 
But each in his own order: Christ, the firstfruits; then those who are Christ's at His coming.

(1 Corinthians 15:24) 
Then comes the end, when He delivers the kingdom to God the Father after He has destroyed every rule and every authority and power.

(1 Corinthians 15:25) 
For He must reign until He has put all His enemies under His feet.

(1 Corinthians 15:26) 
The last enemy to be destroyed is death.

(1 Corinthians 15:27) 
For He has put all things in subjection under His feet. But when He says, “All things are put in subjection,” it is evident that He is excepted who put all things in subjection to Him.

(1 Corinthians 15:28) 
When all things are subjected to Him, then the Son Himself will also be subjected to Him who put all things in subjection to Him, so that God may be all in all.

(1 Corinthians 15:29) 
Otherwise, what will they do who are baptized for the dead? If the dead do not rise at all, why are people baptized for them?

(1 Corinthians 15:30) 
And why are we in danger every hour?

(1 Corinthians 15:31) 
I protest by your boasting, brothers, which I have in Christ Jesus our Lord, that I die every day.

(1 Corinthians 15:32) 
If, after the manner of men, I fought with beasts at Ephesus, what does it profit me? If the dead do not rise, “Let us eat and drink, for tomorrow we die.”

(1 Corinthians 15:33) 
Do not be deceived: “Evil company corrupts good habits.”

(1 Corinthians 15:34) 
Wake up to righteousness and do not sin, for some have no knowledge of God. I say this to your shame.

(1 Corinthians 15:35) 
But someone will say, “How are the dead raised? And with what kind of body do they come?”

(1 Corinthians 15:36) 
Fool! What you sow is not made alive unless it dies.

(1 Corinthians 15:37) 
And what you sow, you do not sow that body which shall be, but a bare grain, perhaps of wheat or some other grain.

(1 Corinthians 15:38) 
But God gives it a body as He has willed, and to each seed a body of its own.

(1 Corinthians 15:39) 
All flesh is not the same flesh, but there is one kind of flesh for humans, another flesh for animals, another for birds, and another for fish.

(1 Corinthians 15:40) 
There are also celestial bodies and terrestrial bodies, but the glory of the celestial is one, and the glory of the terrestrial is another.

(1 Corinthians 15:41) 
There is one glory of the sun, another glory of the moon, and another glory of the stars; for star differs from star in glory.

(1 Corinthians 15:42) 
So also is the resurrection of the dead. It is sown in corruption; it is raised in incorruption.

(1 Corinthians 15:43) 
It is sown in dishonor; it is raised in glory.

(1 Corinthians 15:44) 
It is sown in weakness; it is raised in power.

(1 Corinthians 15:45) 
It is sown a natural body; it is raised a spiritual body. If there is a natural body, there is also a spiritual body.

(1 Corinthians 15:46) 
So also it is written, “The first man, Adam, became a living soul.” The last Adam became a life-giving spirit.

(1 Corinthians 15:47) 
However, the spiritual is not first, but the natural; then the spiritual.

(1 Corinthians 15:48) 
The first man was from the earth, made of dust; the second man is from heaven.

(1 Corinthians 15:49) 
As was the earthly man, so are those who are earthly; and as is the heavenly man, so also are those who are heavenly.

(1 Corinthians 15:50) 
And just as we have borne the image of the earthly, we will also bear the image of the heavenly.

(1 Corinthians 15:51) 
Now this I say, brothers, that flesh and blood cannot inherit the kingdom of God, nor does corruption inherit incorruption.

(1 Corinthians 15:52) 
Behold, I tell you a mystery: We will not all sleep, but we will all be changed,

(1 Corinthians 15:53) 
in a moment, in the twinkling of an eye, at the last trumpet. For the trumpet will sound, and the dead will be raised incorruptible, and we will be changed.

(1 Corinthians 15:54) 
For this corruptible must put on incorruption, and this mortal must put on immortality.

(1 Corinthians 15:55) 
But when this corruptible has put on incorruption, and this mortal has put on immortality, then shall be brought to pass the saying that is written: “Death is swallowed up in victory.”

(1 Corinthians 15:56) 
“O Death, where is your victory? O Hades, where is your sting?”

(1 Corinthians 15:57) 
The sting of death is sin, and the power of sin is the law.

(1 Corinthians 15:58) 
But thanks be to God, who gives us the victory through our Lord Jesus Christ.

(1 Corinthians 15:59) 
Therefore, my beloved brothers, be steadfast, immovable, always abounding in the work of the Lord, knowing that your labor is not in vain in the Lord.

(1 Corinthians 16:1) 
Now, regarding the collection for the saints, just as I directed the churches in Galatia, so also you should do.

(1 Corinthians 16:2) 
On the first day of the week, let each of you put aside and store up whatever he may have been blessed with, so that there be no collections when I come.

(1 Corinthians 16:3) 
And when I arrive, I will send whoever you approve with letters, to carry your gracious gift to Jerusalem.

(1 Corinthians 16:4) 
If it is fitting that I go as well, they will go with me.

(1 Corinthians 16:5) 
I will come to you after I pass through Macedonia, for I intend to pass through Macedonia.

(1 Corinthians 16:6) 
Perhaps I will stay with you for a time, or even spend the winter with you, so that you may send me on my way wherever I go.

(1 Corinthians 16:7) 
For I do not want to see you just in passing; I hope to remain with you for a while, if the Lord allows.

(1 Corinthians 16:8) 
But I will stay in Ephesus until Pentecost.

(1 Corinthians 16:9) 
For a great and effective door has opened for me, and there are many adversaries.

(1 Corinthians 16:10) 
If Timothy comes, see that he is without fear among you, for he is doing the work of the Lord, just as I am.

(1 Corinthians 16:11) 
Therefore, let no one despise him, but send him on his way in peace, that he may come to me. For I am expecting him with the brothers.

(1 Corinthians 16:12) 
Now, concerning our brother Apollos: I strongly urged him to come to you with the brothers, and he was not at all willing to come now; but he will come when he has the opportunity.

(1 Corinthians 16:13) 
Be vigilant, stand firm in the faith, act like men, and be strong.

(1 Corinthians 16:14) 
Let all that you do be done in love.

(1 Corinthians 16:15) 
Now I urge you, brothers: you know that the household of Stephanas, and Fortunatus, and Achaicus, are the first fruits of Achaia, and that they have devoted themselves to the service of the saints.

(1 Corinthians 16:16) 
I ask that you be subject to such people, and to everyone who works and labors with them.

(1 Corinthians 16:17) 
I rejoice at the coming of Stephanas, and Fortunatus, and Achaicus, because they have supplied what was lacking from you.

(1 Corinthians 16:18) 
They have refreshed my spirit and yours. Therefore, acknowledge such people.

(1 Corinthians 16:19) 
The churches of Asia salute you. Aquila and Prisca, together with the church in their house, salute you warmly in the Lord.

(1 Corinthians 16:20) 
All the brothers salute you. Greet one another with a holy kiss.

(1 Corinthians 16:21) 
The greeting is with my own hand—Paul’s.

(1 Corinthians 16:22) 
If anyone does not love the Lord Jesus Christ, let him be accursed. Maran atha!

(1 Corinthians 16:23) 
The grace of our Lord Jesus Christ be with you.

(1 Corinthians 16:24) 
My love be with all of you in Christ Jesus. Amen.

(2 Corinthians 1:1) 
Paul, an Apostle of Jesus Christ, by the will of God, and Timothy, our brother, to the Church of God, which is at Corinth, with all the saints who are in all of Achaia:

(2 Corinthians 1:2) 
May grace and peace be granted to you by God our Father and the Lord Jesus Christ.

(2 Corinthians 1:3) 
Blessed be God the Father of our Lord Jesus Christ, the Father of mercies and God of all consolation,

(2 Corinthians 1:4) 
who comforts us in all our tribulation, so that we may be able to comfort those who are in any trouble, with the comfort with which we ourselves are comforted by God.

(2 Corinthians 1:5) 
For as the sufferings of Christ abound in us, so also our consolation abounds through Christ.

(2 Corinthians 1:6) 
Whether we are afflicted, it is for your exhortation and salvation; or whether we are comforted, it is for your consolation, which produces the endurance of the same sufferings which we also suffer:

(2 Corinthians 1:7) 
so that our hope for you may be steadfast, knowing that as you are partakers of the sufferings, so also are you of the consolation.

(2 Corinthians 1:8) 
For we do not want you to be ignorant, brothers, about our affliction which came upon us in Asia, that we were crushed beyond measure, beyond our strength, so that we despaired even of life.

(2 Corinthians 1:9) 
But we ourselves had the sentence of death within ourselves, so that we would not trust in ourselves but in God, who raises the dead;

(2 Corinthians 1:10) 
who delivered us from so great a death, and does deliver, on whom we have set our hope that He will also deliver us again,

(2 Corinthians 1:11) 
while you also help us by prayer, so that thanks may be given by many persons on our behalf for the gift bestowed on us through the prayers of many.

(2 Corinthians 1:12) 
For our boast is this: the testimony of our conscience, that in simplicity and godly sincerity, not in carnal wisdom but in the grace of God, we have conducted ourselves in the world, and especially toward you.

(2 Corinthians 1:13) 
For we are not writing anything to you other than what you read and understand, and I hope you will understand completely,

(2 Corinthians 1:14) 
as you have also understood us in part, that we are your glory, even as you are ours, in the day of our Lord Jesus.

(2 Corinthians 1:15) 
Because of this confidence I intended to come to you first, so that you might have a second favor,

(2 Corinthians 1:16) 
and to pass through you to Macedonia, and again from Macedonia to come to you, and by you to be brought on my way toward Judea.

(2 Corinthians 1:17) 
When I had planned this, did I do so lightly? Or do I make plans according to the flesh, so that with me there is yes and no?

(2 Corinthians 1:18) 
But as God is faithful, our word to you is not yes and no.

(2 Corinthians 1:19) 
For the Son of God, Jesus Christ, who was preached among you by us, by me and Silvanus and Timothy, was not yes and no, but in Him it was yes.

(2 Corinthians 1:20) 
For as many as are the promises of God, in Him they are yes; therefore also through Him is the Amen, to the glory of God through us.

(2 Corinthians 1:21) 
Now He who establishes us with you in Christ and has anointed us is God,

(2 Corinthians 1:22) 
who also sealed us and gave us the Spirit in our hearts as a pledge.

(2 Corinthians 1:23) 
But I call on God as witness to my soul, that to spare you, I did not come again to Corinth.

(2 Corinthians 1:24) 
Not that we have dominion over your faith, but we are helpers of your joy; for in faith you stand firm.

(2 Corinthians 2:1) 
This is my own decision: I will not visit you with sadness again.

(2 Corinthians 2:2) 
Because if I cause you grief, who is there to make me joyful, except for the one who suffers grief from me?

(2 Corinthians 2:3) 
This is why I wrote to you, so that I will not have grief when I arrive, from those who should be my joy. I have confidence in all of you, because my joy is the joy of you all.

(2 Corinthians 2:4) 
For I wrote to you with great affliction and anguish of heart, through many tears: not to cause you grief, but so you know how much love I have for you.

(2 Corinthians 2:5) 
Now, if anyone has caused grief, it has not been me, but in part, so as not to burden all of you.

(2 Corinthians 2:6) 
It is enough for such a person to be rebuked, as he has been by most of you.

(2 Corinthians 2:7) 
Instead, you should forgive him and console him, lest he is overwhelmed by excessive grief.

(2 Corinthians 2:8) 
So, I ask you to reaffirm your love for him.

(2 Corinthians 2:9) 
I wrote to you for this very purpose: to see if you are obedient in all things.

(2 Corinthians 2:10) 
If you forgive anyone, I also forgive. Because whatever I have forgiven, I have forgiven it for you, in the person of Christ.

(2 Corinthians 2:11) 
So that we are not taken advantage of by Satan, for we are not ignorant of his schemes.

(2 Corinthians 2:12) 
When I went to Troas to preach the Gospel of Christ, and a door was opened for me in the Lord,

(2 Corinthians 2:13) 
I had no rest in my spirit because I didn't find my brother Titus. So I said goodbye to them and set off for Macedonia.

(2 Corinthians 2:14) 
But thanks be to God, who always gives us the victory in Christ, and manifests the fragrance of the knowledge of him in every place.

(2 Corinthians 2:15) 
For we are the aroma of Christ to God in those who are being saved and in those who are perishing:

(2 Corinthians 2:16) 
to some, it is the scent of death leading to death, and to others, the scent of life leading to life. And who is worthy of this?

(2 Corinthians 2:17) 
We are not like so many others who are corrupting the word of God. Instead, we speak with sincerity, from God, before God, in Christ.

(2 Corinthians 3:1) 
Are we now starting again to recommend ourselves? Or do we need, as some, letters of recommendation to you, or from you?

(2 Corinthians 3:2) 
You are our letter of recommendation, written in our hearts, which all men know and read:

(2 Corinthians 3:3) 
It is clear that you are a letter from Christ, prepared through our ministry, written not with ink, but with the Spirit of the living God; not on tablets of stone, but on the tablets of the flesh of the heart.

(2 Corinthians 3:4) 
And such is the confidence that we have through Christ toward God:

(2 Corinthians 3:5) 
Not that we are sufficient to think of anything as from ourselves, but our sufficiency is from God:

(2 Corinthians 3:6) 
Who also made us capable ministers of the New Testament; not of the letter, but of the spirit. For the letter kills, but the spirit gives life.

(2 Corinthians 3:7) 
Now if the ministry of death, engraved in letters on stone, was in glory, so that the children of Israel could not look upon the face of Moses because of the glory of his face, which glory was passing:

(2 Corinthians 3:8) 
How much more will the ministry of the Spirit be with glory?

(2 Corinthians 3:9) 
For if the ministry of condemnation has glory, much more abounds in glory the ministry of justice.

(2 Corinthians 3:10) 
For indeed that which was made glorious has not been glorified in this respect, because of the surpassing glory.

(2 Corinthians 3:11) 
For if that which passes away was glorious, much more that which remains is in glory.

(2 Corinthians 3:12) 
Therefore, having such a hope, we use much confidence:

(2 Corinthians 3:13) 
And not as Moses put a veil over his face, so that the children of Israel could not look at the end of that which was passing.

(2 Corinthians 3:14) 
But their minds were hardened. For until this very day, the same veil in the reading of the Old Testament remains unremoved, because in Christ it is done away.

(2 Corinthians 3:15) 
But even to this day, when Moses is read, the veil is still placed upon their heart.

(2 Corinthians 3:16) 
But when it shall turn to the Lord, the veil shall be taken away.

(2 Corinthians 3:17) 
Now the Lord is the Spirit, and where the Spirit of the Lord is, there is liberty.

(2 Corinthians 3:18) 
But we all, with unveiled face beholding as in a mirror the glory of the Lord, are being transformed into the same image from glory to glory, as by the Spirit of the Lord.

(2 Corinthians 4:1) 
Therefore, since we have received this work of ministry, by God's mercy, we don't give up;

(2 Corinthians 4:2) 
but we avoid the hidden tricks of shame, we don't distort the Word of God, and we speak the truth in the open, recommending ourselves to every human conscience before God.

(2 Corinthians 4:3) 
If our Gospel is veiled, it is hidden from those who are perishing;

(2 Corinthians 4:4) 
in whom the god of this world has blinded the minds of the unbelievers, lest the light of the Gospel of the glory of Christ shine through, who is the image of God.

(2 Corinthians 4:5) 
For we don't preach ourselves, but Jesus Christ Our Lord: but we declare ourselves to be your servants for Jesus' sake.

(2 Corinthians 4:6) 
Because God, who said, "Let light shine out of darkness," has shone in our hearts to enlighten the knowledge of the glory of God in the face of Jesus Christ.

(2 Corinthians 4:7) 
But we have this treasure in clay vessels: so that the preeminence of the power may be of God, and not of us.

(2 Corinthians 4:8) 
In all things we suffer tribulation, but we are not distressed; we are in doubt, but we don't despair;

(2 Corinthians 4:9) 
we are persecuted, but we are not abandoned; we are cast down, but we don't perish:

(2 Corinthians 4:10) 
always carrying about in our body the mortification of Jesus: so that the life of Jesus may be revealed in our bodies.

(2 Corinthians 4:11) 
For we who live are always delivered to death for Jesus' sake: so that the life of Jesus may be revealed in our mortal flesh.

(2 Corinthians 4:12) 
Therefore, death is at work in us, but life in you.

(2 Corinthians 4:13) 
But having the same spirit of faith, as it is written: "I believed, therefore I spoke," we also believe, therefore we speak:

(2 Corinthians 4:14) 
knowing that He who raised up Jesus will raise us also with Jesus and place us with you.

(2 Corinthians 4:15) 
For all things are for you, so that the abundance of grace, by many thanksgivings, may abound to the glory of God.

(2 Corinthians 4:16) 
Therefore we don't give up: but even though our outer man is decaying, our inner man is renewed day by day.

(2 Corinthians 4:17) 
For that which is at present momentary and light of our tribulation, works for us, above all measure, an eternal weight of glory:

(2 Corinthians 4:18) 
as we don't look at the things that are seen, but at the things that are not seen. For the things that are seen are temporal, but the things that are not seen are eternal.

(2 Corinthians 5:1) 
We know that when our earthly body dies, God has a building prepared for us. It's not made by human hands but eternal in heaven.

(2 Corinthians 5:2) 
We groan in our bodies, longing to be clothed in a heavenly dwelling.

(2 Corinthians 5:3) 
We hope that when we are clothed, we are not found naked of good works.

(2 Corinthians 5:4) 
Indeed, we groan under the weight of this tent we call our body. Not that we want to be unclothed but rather clothed in new life, so that what is mortal is swallowed up by life eternal.

(2 Corinthians 5:5) 
God, who prepared us for this, has given us the Holy Spirit as a pledge.

(2 Corinthians 5:6) 
So we are always confident, knowing that while we are in the body, we are away from the Lord.

(2 Corinthians 5:7) 
We walk by faith, not by sight.

(2 Corinthians 5:8) 
We are confident and prefer to be away from the body and at home with the Lord.

(2 Corinthians 5:9) 
So we make it our aim to please Him, whether at home or away.

(2 Corinthians 5:10) 
For we must all appear before the judgment seat of Christ, so that each one may receive what he has done in the body, whether good or bad.

(2 Corinthians 5:11) 
Knowing the fear of the Lord, we try to persuade people, and God knows our hearts. I hope that you understand us too.

(2 Corinthians 5:12) 
We are not commending ourselves to you again, but we are giving you an opportunity to be proud of us, so you can answer those who boast about outward appearance and not their inner hearts.

(2 Corinthians 5:13) 
For whether we are out of our minds, it is for God; or whether we are sober, it is for you.

(2 Corinthians 5:14) 
The love of Christ compels us, because we are convinced that one died for all; therefore all have died.

(2 Corinthians 5:15) 
And He died for all, so that those who live should no longer live for themselves but for Him who died for them and was raised.

(2 Corinthians 5:16) 
From now on, therefore, we regard no one according to the flesh. Even though we once knew Christ according to the flesh, we no longer know Him that way.

(2 Corinthians 5:17) 
Therefore, if anyone is in Christ, he is a new creation; the old has passed away; behold, the new has come.

(2 Corinthians 5:18) 
All this is from God, who reconciled us to Himself through Christ and gave us the ministry of reconciliation.

(2 Corinthians 5:19) 
God was reconciling the world to Himself in Christ, not counting people’s sins against them. And He has committed to us the word of reconciliation.

(2 Corinthians 5:20) 
Therefore, we are ambassadors for Christ, God making His appeal through us. We implore you on behalf of Christ, be reconciled to God.

(2 Corinthians 5:21) 
For our sake He made Him to be sin who knew no sin, so that in Him we might become the righteousness of God.

(2 Corinthians 6:1) 
We are working together, and we urge you not to receive the grace of God in vain.

(2 Corinthians 6:2) 
For He says, "In an acceptable time, I have heard you, and in the day of salvation, I have helped you." Behold, now is the acceptable time; behold, now is the day of salvation.

(2 Corinthians 6:3) 
We give no offense to anyone, so that the ministry may not be blamed.

(2 Corinthians 6:4) 
But in everything, we are showing ourselves to be ministers of God: through much patience, in tribulations, in needs, in distresses,

(2 Corinthians 6:5) 
in beatings, in imprisonments, in riots, in labors, in watchings, in fastings,

(2 Corinthians 6:6) 
in purity, in knowledge, in longsuffering, in kindness, in the Holy Spirit, in love unfeigned,

(2 Corinthians 6:7) 
in the word of truth, in the power of God: through the weapons of justice on the right and on the left,

(2 Corinthians 6:8) 
through glory and dishonor, through ill repute and good repute. We are treated as deceivers, and yet we are truthful;

(2 Corinthians 6:9) 
as unknown, and yet we are well-known; as dying, and behold, we live; as punished, and yet not killed;

(2 Corinthians 6:10) 
as sorrowful, yet always rejoicing; as poor, yet enriching many; as having nothing, and yet possessing everything.

(2 Corinthians 6:11) 
Our mouth is open to you, O Corinthians; our heart is enlarged.

(2 Corinthians 6:12) 
You are not limited in us, but you are limited in your own affections.

(2 Corinthians 6:13) 
Now for the same recompense (I speak as to my children), be you also enlarged.

(2 Corinthians 6:14) 
Do not be yoked with unbelievers. For what partnership has righteousness with lawlessness? Or what fellowship does light have with darkness?

(2 Corinthians 6:15) 
What harmony does Christ have with Belial? Or what does a believer share with an unbeliever?

(2 Corinthians 6:16) 
What agreement does the temple of God have with idols? For you are the temple of the living God, as God has said: "I will dwell in them and walk among them, and I will be their God, and they will be my people."

(2 Corinthians 6:17) 
Therefore, "Come out from among them, and be separate," says the Lord, "and touch no unclean thing. And I will receive you,"

(2 Corinthians 6:18) 
"And I will be a Father to you, and you will be sons and daughters to me," says the Lord Almighty.

(2 Corinthians 7:1) 
Since we have God's promises, beloved ones, let us purify ourselves from all sin, which stains the flesh and the soul. Let us finish the work of spiritual growth, which is born of reverent fear of God.

(2 Corinthians 7:2) 
Open up your hearts to us. We haven’t harmed anyone. We haven’t corrupted anyone. We haven’t taken advantage of anyone.

(2 Corinthians 7:3) 
I don’t mean to accuse anyone. I’ve already said that you have a place in our hearts, for us to live and die with.

(2 Corinthians 7:4) 
I have great confidence in you. I am very proud of you. I am overflowing with consolation, and I am filled with joy in the midst of all our suffering.

(2 Corinthians 7:5) 
Because when we came to Macedonia, we got no rest. We were attacked on all sides. There was conflict all around us, and anxiety within.

(2 Corinthians 7:6) 
But God, who comforts the afflicted, comforted us when Titus arrived.

(2 Corinthians 7:7) 
His arrival wasn’t the only comfort, but we were consoled by the comfort he received from you. He told us about your longing to see us, your grief, and your zeal for me, so that I was even more joyful.

(2 Corinthians 7:8) 
Even though I saddened you in the letter, I don’t regret it. I do regret it, because that letter, although it was painful for a time, did sadden you.

(2 Corinthians 7:9) 
Now I am joyful, not because you were saddened, but because you were saddened to the point of repentance. Because you were saddened in the right way, according to God's will, so that you suffered no loss from us.

(2 Corinthians 7:10) 
For grief that is according to God brings repentance that leads to salvation, which will never be regretted. But the grief of the world brings death.

(2 Corinthians 7:11) 
See what this very thing—that you were saddened in the right way, according to God's will—has produced in you: great diligence, a defense of your character, indignation against sin, fear of God, longing to be reconciled, zeal for doing good, and a readiness to punish the offender. You have shown yourselves to be blameless in the matter.

(2 Corinthians 7:12) 
So, even though I wrote the letter, it wasn’t for the sake of the one who did wrong or the one who was wronged. I wrote so that you might understand the great care we have for you, as shown in the sight of God.

(2 Corinthians 7:13) 
This is why we were comforted. And in our comfort, we rejoiced even more because of Titus’s joy, for his spirit was refreshed by you all.

(2 Corinthians 7:14) 
For if I had boasted to him about you, I was not ashamed, but just as everything we said to you was true, so also our boasting about you to Titus has also proven to be true.

(2 Corinthians 7:15) 
And his heart is overflowing with affection for you as he remembers the obedience of you all, how you received him with fear and trembling.

(2 Corinthians 7:16) 
I am rejoicing that I have complete confidence in you in every way.

(2 Corinthians 8:1) 
We want you to know, brothers, about the grace of God given to the churches in Macedonia:

(2 Corinthians 8:2) 
During their great suffering, the overflowing joy and their extreme poverty were able to abound in the riches of their generosity.

(2 Corinthians 8:3) 
For I testify that they gave according to their ability and even beyond their ability; they were willing, even beyond their means,

(2 Corinthians 8:4) 
begging us with great insistence for the grace of participating in the service to the saints.

(2 Corinthians 8:5) 
And this was more than we expected, because they gave themselves first to God and then to us, by the will of God.

(2 Corinthians 8:6) 
So we urged Titus to finish what he had started. He was the one who started the grace of giving.

(2 Corinthians 8:7) 
But since you abound in everything, in faith, in speech, in knowledge, in all diligence, and in your love for us, may you also abound in this grace.

(2 Corinthians 8:8) 
I am not commanding you, but I am testing the sincerity of your love by comparing it to the diligence of others.

(2 Corinthians 8:9) 
For you know the grace of our Lord Jesus Christ; though He was rich, for your sake He became poor, so that through His poverty you might become rich.

(2 Corinthians 8:10) 
And I give my judgment in this matter: it is to your advantage to finish what you began a year ago, and to do so with enthusiasm.

(2 Corinthians 8:11) 
Now, finish doing it, so that your readiness to give may be matched by your eagerness to give out of what you have.

(2 Corinthians 8:12) 
If the willingness is there, the offering is acceptable according to what one has, not according to what one does not have.

(2 Corinthians 8:13) 
For I do not want you to be burdened while others are relieved, but that there should be equality.

(2 Corinthians 8:14) 
At the present time, your abundance should supply their need, so that their abundance may also supply your need; then there will be equality.

(2 Corinthians 8:15) 
As it is written, “The one who gathered much did not have too much, and the one who gathered little did not have too little.”

(2 Corinthians 8:16) 
But thanks be to God, who put the same diligence for you into the heart of Titus.

(2 Corinthians 8:17) 
For he accepted the exhortation, but he is even more diligent and comes to you of his own accord.

(2 Corinthians 8:18) 
We are sending along with him the brother who is praised by all the churches for his work in the Gospel.

(2 Corinthians 8:19) 
Moreover, he was appointed by the churches to travel with us as we administer this grace for the glory of the Lord and to show our eagerness to help.

(2 Corinthians 8:20) 
We are careful to avoid any criticism of the way we administer this generous offering.

(2 Corinthians 8:21) 
We are taking pains to do what is right, not only in the eyes of the Lord but also in the eyes of others.

(2 Corinthians 8:22) 
We are sending along with them our brother, whom we have often tested in many matters and found eager, but who is now even more eager because of his great trust in you.

(2 Corinthians 8:23) 
As for Titus, he is my partner and fellow worker for your benefit. As for our brothers, they are apostles of the churches, the glory of Christ.

(2 Corinthians 8:24) 
Therefore, show these men the proof of your love and of our reason for boasting about you, before the face of the churches.

(2 Corinthians 9:1) 
Now concerning the ministry to the saints, it's unnecessary for me to write to you about it.

(2 Corinthians 9:2) 
For I know your willing spirit, of which I boast about you to the Macedonians, that Achaia has been ready since last year. And your enthusiasm has stirred up many others.

(2 Corinthians 9:3) 
I sent the brothers so that our boasting about you might not be in vain in this regard, but that, as I said, you might be prepared.

(2 Corinthians 9:4) 
Otherwise, when I come with the Macedonians and find you unprepared, we (not to say you) would be ashamed in this matter.

(2 Corinthians 9:5) 
Therefore, I considered it necessary to ask the brothers to go ahead of you to you, and prepare this promised blessing, so that it may be ready as a blessing and not as a matter of greed.

(2 Corinthians 9:6) 
I say this: The one who sows sparingly will also reap sparingly; and the one who sows generously will also reap generously.

(2 Corinthians 9:7) 
Each one must give as they have determined in their heart, not reluctantly or out of compulsion, for God loves a cheerful giver.

(2 Corinthians 9:8) 
And God is able to make all grace abound toward you, so that in all things at all times, having all that you need, you may abound in every good work.

(2 Corinthians 9:9) 
As it is written, "He has scattered abroad, He has given to the poor; His righteousness endures forever."

(2 Corinthians 9:10) 
Now He who supplies seed to the sower and bread for food will supply and multiply your seed for sowing and increase the harvest of your righteousness.

(2 Corinthians 9:11) 
You will be enriched in every way so that you can be generous on every occasion, and through us your generosity will result in thanksgiving to God.

(2 Corinthians 9:12) 
For this service of ministering to the needs of the saints is not only supplying the needs of the saints but is also abounding with many thanksgivings to God.

(2 Corinthians 9:13) 
Through the proof of this service, they will glorify God for your obedience to the confession of the Gospel of Christ, and for your generosity in sharing with them and with everyone.

(2 Corinthians 9:14) 
And in their prayers for you, they long for you because of the surpassing grace of God in you.

(2 Corinthians 9:15) 
Thanks be to God for His inexpressible gift!

(2 Corinthians 10:1) 
And I, Paul, now implore you by the gentleness and humility of Christ. Some people say I seem weak when I am with you in person, but in my absence, I am a stern teacher.

(2 Corinthians 10:2) 
I beg you not to force me to be bold in my teaching. Some say I walk in worldly ways.

(2 Corinthians 10:3) 
Even though we live in the flesh, we do not wage war according to the flesh.

(2 Corinthians 10:4) 
The weapons we fight with are not those of this world, but they have divine power to demolish strongholds. We demolish arguments,

(2 Corinthians 10:5) 
and every pretension that is raised up against the knowledge of God, and we take captive every thought to make it obedient to Christ.

(2 Corinthians 10:6) 
And we will be ready to punish every act of disobedience when your obedience is complete.

(2 Corinthians 10:7) 
You are judging by mere appearances. If anyone is confident that they belong to Christ, they should consider again that we belong to Christ just as much as they do.

(2 Corinthians 10:8) 
Even if I boast somewhat more about the authority the Lord gave us for building you up rather than tearing you down, I will not be ashamed.

(2 Corinthians 10:9) 
I do not want you to think I am trying to frighten you with my letters.

(2 Corinthians 10:10) 
Some say, “His letters are weighty and forceful, but in person, he is weak, and his speech is of no account.”

(2 Corinthians 10:11) 
Such people should realize that what we are in our letters when we are absent, we will be in our actions when we are present.

(2 Corinthians 10:12) 
We do not dare to classify or compare ourselves with some who commend themselves. When they measure themselves by themselves and compare themselves with themselves, they are not wise.

(2 Corinthians 10:13) 
We, however, will not boast beyond measure, but will keep within the limits of the sphere God has assigned to us, a sphere that reaches even to you.

(2 Corinthians 10:14) 
We are not going too far in our boasting, since we were the first to come to you with the gospel of Christ.

(2 Corinthians 10:15) 
We do not boast beyond measure of other people’s labor, but we hope that as your faith increases, our sphere of activity among you will be enlarged.

(2 Corinthians 10:16) 
We want to preach the gospel to you even more, and go to places beyond you, without boasting in what has already been done in someone else's sphere.

(2 Corinthians 10:17) 
Let the one who boasts, boast in the Lord.

(2 Corinthians 10:18) 
For it is not the one who commends himself who is approved, but the one whom the Lord commends.

(2 Corinthians 11:1) 
I wish you would put up with just a little bit of my foolishness! But please bear with me.

(2 Corinthians 11:2) 
I am zealous for you with the zeal of God. I betrothed you to one husband, to present you as a chaste virgin to Christ.

(2 Corinthians 11:3) 
But I am afraid that, as the serpent deceived Eve by his cunning, your thoughts may be corrupted and led astray from a sincere and pure devotion to Christ.

(2 Corinthians 11:4) 
For if anyone comes and preaches another Jesus, whom we did not preach, or if you receive a different spirit from the one you received, or a different gospel from the one you accepted, you put up with it very well.

(2 Corinthians 11:5) 
For I consider that I am in no way inferior to these super-apostles.

(2 Corinthians 11:6) 
Even if I am unskilled in speech, I am not unskilled in knowledge. But in every way we have been fully manifested among you.

(2 Corinthians 11:7) 
Or did I commit a sin by humbling myself so that you might be exalted, because I preached the Gospel of God to you free of charge?

(2 Corinthians 11:8) 
I robbed other churches, taking wages from them to serve you.

(2 Corinthians 11:9) 
And when I was present with you and was in need, I did not burden anyone. The brothers who came from Macedonia supplied what I lacked, and in everything I have kept myself, and will keep myself, from being a burden to you.

(2 Corinthians 11:10) 
As the truth of Christ is in me, this boasting will not be silenced in me in the regions of Achaia.

(2 Corinthians 11:11) 
Why? Because I do not love you? God knows!

(2 Corinthians 11:12) 
But what I am doing, I will continue to do, in order to cut off the opportunity of those who want an opportunity to be regarded as we are in what they boast about.

(2 Corinthians 11:13) 
For such men are false apostles, deceitful workmen, disguising themselves as apostles of Christ.

(2 Corinthians 11:14) 
And no wonder, for even Satan disguises himself as an angel of light.

(2 Corinthians 11:15) 
So it is no surprise if his servants also disguise themselves as servants of righteousness, whose end will be according to their works.

(2 Corinthians 11:16) 
I say again: Let no one think me foolish. But if you do, then receive me as a fool, so that I too may boast a little.

(2 Corinthians 11:17) 
What I am saying, I am not saying as the Lord would, but as it were, in foolishness, in this confidence of boasting.

(2 Corinthians 11:18) 
Since many boast according to the flesh, I too will boast.

(2 Corinthians 11:19) 
For you gladly put up with fools, being as you are so wise!

(2 Corinthians 11:20) 
For you put up with it if anyone enslaves you, if anyone devours you, if anyone takes advantage of you, if anyone exalts himself, if anyone strikes you in the face.

(2 Corinthians 11:21) 
I say this to my shame, as though we were weak. But in whatever anyone dares to boast (I am speaking in foolishness), I also dare to boast.

(2 Corinthians 11:22) 
Are they Hebrews? So am I. Are they Israelites? So am I. Are they descendants of Abraham? So am I.

(2 Corinthians 11:23) 
Are they servants of Christ? (I am speaking as a fool.) I am more so, with far greater labors, with far more imprisonments, with countless beatings, and often near death.

(2 Corinthians 11:24) 
Five times I received from the Jews the forty lashes minus one.

(2 Corinthians 11:25) 
Three times I was beaten with rods, I was stoned once, three times I was shipwrecked, and I have spent a night and a day in the open sea.

(2 Corinthians 11:26) 
In journeys often, dangers from rivers, dangers from robbers, dangers from my own people, dangers from Gentiles, dangers in the city, dangers in the wilderness, dangers at sea, dangers among false brothers.

(2 Corinthians 11:27) 
In labor and hardship, through sleepless nights, in hunger and thirst, often in fasting, in cold and nakedness.

(2 Corinthians 11:28) 
And besides other things, there is the daily pressure on me of my anxiety for all the churches.

(2 Corinthians 11:29) 
Who is weak, and I am not weak? Who is led into sin, and I do not burn with anger?

(2 Corinthians 11:30) 
If I must boast, I will boast of the things that show my weakness.

(2 Corinthians 11:31) 
The God and Father of our Lord Jesus Christ, who is blessed forever, knows that I am not lying.

(2 Corinthians 11:32) 
In Damascus the governor under King Aretas was guarding the city of Damascus in order to arrest me.

(2 Corinthians 11:33) 
But I was let down in a basket through a window in the wall and escaped his hands.

(2 Corinthians 12:1) 
It is necessary for me to boast, though I shouldn't. But I will now speak about the visions and revelations of the Lord.

(2 Corinthians 12:2) 
I know a man in Christ, who was taken up fourteen years ago to the third atmosphere—I do not know whether in the body, or out of the body, God knows.

(2 Corinthians 12:3) 
And I know that this man, whether in the body or out of the body, I do not know, God knows,

(2 Corinthians 12:4) 
was snatched up into Paradise. He heard things that cannot be spoken, that no man is allowed to utter.

(2 Corinthians 12:5) 
I will boast about this man. I will not boast about myself, except in my weaknesses.

(2 Corinthians 12:6) 
For even if I wanted to boast, I would not be foolish, for I will speak the truth. But I forbear, lest any man should think of me above that which he sees in me, or that he hears of me.

(2 Corinthians 12:7) 
And lest the magnitude of the revelations should lift me up, there was given to me a thorn in the flesh, an angel of Satan, to buffet me.

(2 Corinthians 12:8) 
Concerning this, I besought the Lord thrice, that it might depart from me.

(2 Corinthians 12:9) 
And He said to me: “My grace is sufficient for you, for power is made perfect in weakness.” Gladly therefore will I glory in my infirmities, that the power of Christ may dwell in me.

(2 Corinthians 12:10) 
Therefore, I take pleasure in infirmities, in reproaches, in necessities, in persecutions, in distresses for Christ's sake. For when I am weak, then I am strong.

(2 Corinthians 12:11) 
I have become foolish, you have compelled me. For I ought to have been recommended by you: for I was no way inferior to the most eminent apostles, although I am nothing.

(2 Corinthians 12:12) 
For the signs of an apostle were wrought among you, in all patience, in signs, and wonders, and mighty deeds.

(2 Corinthians 12:13) 
For what is there that you were inferior to other churches? Except that I myself have not been a burden to you. Forgive me this injury.

(2 Corinthians 12:14) 
Behold, I am ready to come to you the third time, and I will not be a burden to you. For I seek not yours, but you. For neither ought the children to lay up for the parents, but the parents for the children.

(2 Corinthians 12:15) 
But I most gladly will spend and be spent for your souls. Though loving you more, I am loved less.

(2 Corinthians 12:16) 
But be it so: I did not burden you: but, being crafty, I caught you with guile.

(2 Corinthians 12:17) 
Did I then make a gain of you by any of them whom I sent to you?

(2 Corinthians 12:18) 
I desired Titus, and I sent a brother with him: did Titus make a gain of you? Did we not walk in the same spirit? Did we not walk in the same steps?

(2 Corinthians 12:19) 
Do you think that all along we are excusing ourselves to you? In the sight of God we speak in Christ: but all things, dearly beloved, for your edification.

(2 Corinthians 12:20) 
For I fear lest, when I come, I shall not find you such as I would, and that I shall be found by you such as you would not. Lest perhaps contentions, jealousies, angers, quarrels, detractions, whisperings, swellings of pride, seditions:

(2 Corinthians 12:21) 
Lest, when I come again, God humiliate me among you: and I mourn many of those who before have sinned and have not done penance for the uncleanness and fornication and lasciviousness that they have committed.

(2 Corinthians 13:1) 
This is the third time I am coming to you. Every matter must be confirmed by the word of two or three witnesses.

(2 Corinthians 13:2) 
I have said this before to those present, and I will say it again to those who are not here, that if I come again, I will not spare you,

(2 Corinthians 13:3) 
because you seek proof that Christ is speaking through me. Christ is not weak in you, but rather, He is strong in you.

(2 Corinthians 13:4) 
For even though He was crucified in weakness, He lives by the power of God. For we also are weak in Him, but we will live with Him by the power of God within you.

(2 Corinthians 13:5) 
Test yourselves to see if you are living in the faith. Examine yourselves. Or do you not know this about yourselves, that Jesus Christ is in you, unless you are reprobate?

(2 Corinthians 13:6) 
But I trust that you will recognize that we are not reprobate.

(2 Corinthians 13:7) 
And we pray to God that you may do no evil, not that we should appear approved, but rather, that you should do what is good, even if we are considered reprobate.

(2 Corinthians 13:8) 
For we can do nothing against the truth, but only for the truth.

(2 Corinthians 13:9) 
For we rejoice when we are weak: we pray for your perfection.

(2 Corinthians 13:10) 
Therefore, I write these things while absent, so that when I am present, I do not have to act severely, according to the power which the Lord gave me for building up, and not for destroying.

(2 Corinthians 13:11) 
Finally, brothers, rejoice, be perfect, be comforted, be of one mind, have peace, and the God of peace and love will be with you.

(2 Corinthians 13:12) 
Greet one another with a holy kiss.

(2 Corinthians 13:13) 
All the saints greet you.

(2 Corinthians 13:14) 
The grace of our Lord Jesus Christ, the love of God, and the fellowship of the Holy Spirit be with you all. Amen.

(Galatians 1:1) 
Paul, a sent one (not appointed by humans, nor through a human intermediary, but through Jesus Christ and God the Father, who raised him from the dead),

(Galatians 1:2) 
and all the brothers who are with me, to the churches of Galatia.

(Galatians 1:3) 
May grace and peace be given to you from God the Father and from the Lord Jesus Christ,

(Galatians 1:4) 
who gave Himself to atone for our sins so that we might be rescued from this present evil world, according to the will of God our Father,

(Galatians 1:5) 
to whom be the glory forever and ever. Amen.

(Galatians 1:6) 
I am astonished that you are so quickly deserting Him who called you to experience the grace of Christ, in order to follow a different gospel;

(Galatians 1:7) 
which is not really a gospel at all; some people are troubling you, and want to change the gospel of Christ.

(Galatians 1:8) 
But even if we, or an angel from heaven, were to evangelize to you anything other than what we evangelized to you, may he be cursed.

(Galatians 1:9) 
As we have said before, so I now say again: If anyone evangelizes to you anything beyond what you have already received, may he be cursed.

(Galatians 1:10) 
Am I now trying to win the favor of men, or of God? Or am I striving to please men? If I were still trying to please men, I would not be a servant of Christ.

(Galatians 1:11) 
For I would have you know, brothers, that the gospel that was evangelized by me is not a human invention.

(Galatians 1:12) 
I did not receive it from any human, nor was I taught it, but it came through a revelation of Jesus Christ.

(Galatians 1:13) 
For you have heard of my former way of life in Judaism: how I persecuted the Church of God beyond measure and tried to destroy it.

(Galatians 1:14) 
And I was advancing in Judaism beyond many of my own age among my people, being more exceedingly zealous for the traditions of my fathers.

(Galatians 1:15) 
But when it pleased Him Who set me apart from birth, and called me through His grace,

(Galatians 1:16) 
to reveal His Son in me, so that I might evangelize Him among the Gentiles, I did not immediately consult with flesh and blood,

(Galatians 1:17) 
nor did I go up to Jerusalem to those who were apostles before me; rather, I went away into Arabia, and returned again to Damascus.

(Galatians 1:18) 
Then after three years I went up to Jerusalem to see Peter, and stayed with him for fifteen days.

(Galatians 1:19) 
But I saw none of the other apostles except James, the brother of the Lord.

(Galatians 1:20) 
In what I am writing to you, before God, I do not lie.

(Galatians 1:21) 
Then I went into the regions of Syria and Cilicia.

(Galatians 1:22) 
And I was still unknown in face to the churches of Judea that were in Christ:

(Galatians 1:23) 
they only heard: “The one who formerly persecuted us is now evangelizing the faith that he once tried to destroy.”

(Galatians 1:24) 
And they were glorifying God in me.

(Galatians 2:1) 
Then after fourteen years, I returned to Jerusalem with Barnabas, bringing along Titus as well.

(Galatians 2:2) 
I went up because of a revelation. I presented the Gospel that I preach to the Gentiles, but I did so privately to those who seemed to be important leaders, to be certain that I wasn't running in vain.

(Galatians 2:3) 
But even Titus, who was with me, was not forced to be circumcised, even though he was a Greek.

(Galatians 2:4) 
This was because of certain false brothers who were secretly brought in. They were trying to find out about the freedom we have in Christ Jesus, to put us back into slavery.

(Galatians 2:5) 
We did not yield to these men for a single hour, nor did we give in to them. We did this so the truth of the Gospel would remain with you.

(Galatians 2:6) 
And from those who seemed to be something, it makes no difference to me what they once were—God shows no partiality. These so-called leaders added nothing to my Gospel.

(Galatians 2:7) 
On the contrary, they saw that I had been entrusted with the Gospel for the uncircumcised, just as Peter had been entrusted with the Gospel for the circumcised.

(Galatians 2:8) 
(For the one who worked through Peter in his ministry to the circumcised also worked through me among the Gentiles:)

(Galatians 2:9) 
And when James, Cephas, and John, who seemed to be pillars, recognized the grace that had been given to me, they gave to Barnabas and me the right hand of fellowship. They agreed that we should go to the Gentiles, and they to the circumcised.

(Galatians 2:10) 
All they asked was that we should remember the poor, which is what I was very eager to do.

(Galatians 2:11) 
But when Cephas came to Antioch, I opposed him to his face, because he stood condemned.

(Galatians 2:12) 
Before certain men came from James, Peter used to eat with the Gentiles. But when they arrived, he began to draw back and separate himself, because he was afraid of those who belonged to the circumcision group.

(Galatians 2:13) 
The other Jews joined him in his hypocrisy, so that even Barnabas was led astray by their hypocrisy.

(Galatians 2:14) 
When I saw that they were not acting in line with the truth of the Gospel, I said to Cephas in front of everyone, “If you, who are a Jew, live like a Gentile and not like a Jew, how can you force Gentiles to live like Jews?

(Galatians 2:15) 
We are Jews by birth, and not sinners from among the Gentiles;

(Galatians 2:16) 
yet we know that a person is not justified by the works of the law, but by faith in Jesus Christ. So we, too, have believed in Christ Jesus, that we may be justified by faith in Christ and not by the works of the law, because by the works of the law no one will be justified.

(Galatians 2:17) 
But if, in seeking to be justified in Christ, we ourselves are found to be sinners, then does that mean Christ promotes sin? Absolutely not!

(Galatians 2:18) 
For if I rebuild what I have destroyed, I become a transgressor.

(Galatians 2:19) 
For through the law I died to the law, so that I might live for God. I have been crucified with Christ.

(Galatians 2:20) 
It is no longer I who live, but Christ who lives in me. And the life I now live in the flesh I live by faith in the Son of God, who loved me and gave himself for me.

(Galatians 2:21) 
I do not set aside the grace of God, for if righteousness could be gained through the law, Christ died for nothing!

(Galatians 3:1) 
O you foolish Galatians! Who has bewitched you, that you should not obey the truth, before whose eyes Jesus Christ was presented, crucified among you?

(Galatians 3:2) 
This only I want to learn from you: Did you receive the Spirit by the works of the Law, or by the hearing of faith?

(Galatians 3:3) 
Are you so foolish? Having begun in the Spirit, are you now being perfected by the flesh?

(Galatians 3:4) 
Have you suffered so many things in vain? If it is indeed in vain.

(Galatians 3:5) 
He therefore who supplies the Spirit to you and works miracles among you, does He do it by the works of the Law, or by the hearing of faith?

(Galatians 3:6) 
As Abraham believed God, and it was accounted to him for righteousness.

(Galatians 3:7)
