Know therefore that those who are of faith, are the sons of Abraham.

(Galatians 3:8) 
And the Scripture, foreseeing that God would justify the Gentiles by faith, announced to Abraham: “In you shall all the nations be blessed.”

(Galatians 3:9) 
Therefore those who are of faith are blessed with faithful Abraham.

(Galatians 3:10) 
For as many as are of the works of the Law are under a curse; for it is written: “Cursed is everyone who does not continue in all things which are written in the book of the Law, to do them.”

(Galatians 3:11) 
But that by the Law no one is justified with God is clear, for “the just man lives by faith.”

(Galatians 3:12) 
But the Law is not of faith, but “he who does them shall live in them.”

(Galatians 3:13) 
Christ has redeemed us from the curse of the Law, having been made a curse for us, for it is written: “Cursed is everyone who hangs on a tree,”

(Galatians 3:14) 
so that the blessing of Abraham might come upon the Gentiles in Christ Jesus, that we might receive the promise of the Spirit through faith.

(Galatians 3:15) 
Brothers, I speak in human terms: even though it is only a man’s covenant, when it has been ratified, no one annuls it or adds to it.

(Galatians 3:16) 
Now to Abraham and his seed were the promises made. He does not say, “And to seeds,” as referring to many, but as to one, “And to your seed,” who is Christ.

(Galatians 3:17) 
Now I say this: The Law, which came four hundred and thirty years later, does not annul a covenant previously ratified by God, so as to make the promise invalid.

(Galatians 3:18) 
For if the inheritance is of the Law, it is no longer of promise; but God granted it to Abraham through promise.

(Galatians 3:19) 
Why then the Law? It was added because of transgressions, until the Seed should come to whom the promise was made, having been ordained through angels in the hand of a mediator.

(Galatians 3:20) 
Now a mediator is not for one only, but God is one.

(Galatians 3:21) 
Is the Law then against the promises of God? By no means! For if a law had been given which could give life, then righteousness would indeed be by the Law.

(Galatians 3:22) 
But the Scripture has confined all things under sin, that the promise by faith in Jesus Christ might be given to those who believe.

(Galatians 3:23) 
But before faith came, we were kept under the Law, confined until the faith which was to be revealed would come.

(Galatians 3:24) 
Therefore the Law was our tutor in Christ, that we might be justified by faith.

(Galatians 3:25) 
But now that faith has come, we are no longer under a tutor.

(Galatians 3:26) 
For you are all sons of God through faith in Christ Jesus.

(Galatians 3:27) 
For as many of you as were baptized into Christ, have put on Christ.

(Galatians 3:28) 
There is neither Jew nor Greek; there is neither slave nor free; there is neither male nor female; for you are all one in Christ Jesus.

(Galatians 3:29) 
And if you are Christ’s, then you are Abraham’s seed, and heirs according to the promise.

(Galatians 4:1) 
I mean, as long as the heir is a child, he is no different from a servant, even though he owns everything,

(Galatians 4:2) 
but he is under guardians and managers until the time fixed by his father.

(Galatians 4:3) 
So too, when we were children, we were enslaved to the basic principles of this world.

(Galatians 4:4) 
But when the time had fully come, God sent forth the Son on a mission by God, born of a woman, born under the Law,

(Galatians 4:5) 
to redeem those who were under the Law, so that we might receive adoption as sons.

(Galatians 4:6) 
And because you are sons, God sent the Spirit of His Son on a mission by God into our hearts, crying out, “Abba! Father!”

(Galatians 4:7) 
So you are no longer a slave, but a son; and if a son, then an heir through God.

(Galatians 4:8) 
However, formerly, when you did not know God, you were enslaved to those who by nature are not gods.

(Galatians 4:9) 
But now that you have known God, or rather have been known by God, how can you turn back again to the weak and beggarly elemental spirits? Do you want to be enslaved to them again?

(Galatians 4:10) 
You observe days and months and seasons and years.

(Galatians 4:11) 
I fear for you, that perhaps I have labored over you in vain.

(Galatians 4:12) 
Become like me, because I also became like you, brothers. I beg you: you have done me no wrong.

(Galatians 4:13) 
You know that because of a physical illness I preached the gospel to you at first.

(Galatians 4:14) 
And though my condition was a trial for you, you did not despise or reject me, but received me as an angel of God, as Christ Jesus.

(Galatians 4:15) 
What has become of your blessedness? For I testify that, if possible, you would have plucked out your eyes and given them to me.

(Galatians 4:16) 
So have I become your enemy by telling you the truth?

(Galatians 4:17) 
They make much of you, but not in a good way; they want to shut you out, so that you will make much of them.

(Galatians 4:18) 
It is always good to be made much of, in a good way, and not only when I am present with you,

(Galatians 4:19) 
My children, for whom I am again in the pain of childbirth until Christ is formed in you!

(Galatians 4:20) 
I wish I could be present with you now and change my tone, because I am perplexed about you.

(Galatians 4:21) 
Tell me, you who want to be under the Law, do you not listen to the Law?

(Galatians 4:22) 
For it is written that Abraham had two sons, one by a slave woman and one by a free woman.

(Galatians 4:23) 
But the son of the slave woman was born according to the flesh, while the son of the free woman was born through promise.

(Galatians 4:24) 
This is an allegory: for these women are two covenants. One is from Mount Sinai, bearing children for slavery; she is Hagar.

(Galatians 4:25) 
Now Hagar is Mount Sinai in Arabia; she corresponds to the present Jerusalem, for she is in slavery with her children.

(Galatians 4:26) 
But the Jerusalem above is free, and she is our mother.

(Galatians 4:27) 
For it is written, “Rejoice, O barren one who does not bear; break forth and cry aloud, you who are not in labor; for the children of the desolate one are more than those of the one who has a husband.”

(Galatians 4:28) 
Now you, brothers, like Isaac, are children of promise.

(Galatians 4:29) 
But just as at that time he who was born according to the flesh persecuted him who was born according to the Spirit, so also now.

(Galatians 4:30) 
But what does the Scripture say? “Cast out the slave woman and her son, for the son of the slave woman shall not inherit with the son of the free woman.”

(Galatians 4:31) 
So, brothers, we are not children of the slave woman but of the free woman.

(Galatians 5:1) 
Be free, therefore! Christ freed us. Do not be enslaved again.

(Galatians 5:2) 
I, Paul, say this: if you are circumcised, Christ will not benefit you in any way.

(Galatians 5:3) 
I testify again to any man who is circumcised that he is obligated to keep the whole Law.

(Galatians 5:4) 
You have been severed from Christ, all of you who try to become justified by the Law; you have fallen from grace.

(Galatians 5:5) 
We eagerly await through the Spirit, by faith, the hope of righteousness.

(Galatians 5:6) 
For in Christ Jesus, neither circumcision nor uncircumcision counts for anything, but only faith working through love.

(Galatians 5:7) 
You were running well. Who stopped you from obeying the truth?

(Galatians 5:8) 
This kind of persuasion does not come from the One who called you.

(Galatians 5:9) 
A little bit of yeast leavens the whole lump.

(Galatians 5:10) 
I am confident in you in the Lord that you will think in no other way; but the one who is troubling you will pay the penalty, whoever he may be.

(Galatians 5:11) 
As for me, brothers, if I still preach circumcision, why am I still persecuted? Then the stumbling block of the cross has been removed.

(Galatians 5:12) 
I wish those who unsettle you would castrate themselves!

(Galatians 5:13) 
For you were called to freedom, brothers. But do not use this freedom as an opportunity for the flesh; rather, serve one another through love.

(Galatians 5:14) 
For the whole Law is fulfilled in one statement: “You shall love your neighbor as yourself.”

(Galatians 5:15) 
But if you bite and devour one another, see that you are not consumed by one another.

(Galatians 5:16) 
But I say: walk in the Spirit, and do not gratify the desires of the flesh.

(Galatians 5:17) 
For the flesh has desires against the Spirit, and the Spirit against the flesh; for these are opposed to each other, so that you do not do what you want.

(Galatians 5:18) 
But if you are led by the Spirit, you are not under the Law.

(Galatians 5:19) 
Now the works of the flesh are obvious: immorality, impurity, licentiousness,

(Galatians 5:20) 
idolatry, sorcery, hatreds, rivalry, jealousy, outbursts of anger, selfish ambitions, dissensions, factions,

(Galatians 5:21) 
envy, drunkenness, carousing, and things like these. I am warning you, as I warned you before: those who do such things will not inherit the kingdom of God.

(Galatians 5:22) 
But the fruit of the Spirit is love, joy, peace, patience, kindness, goodness, faithfulness, gentleness, self-control;

(Galatians 5:23) 
against such things there is no law.

(Galatians 5:24) 
Now those who belong to Christ Jesus have crucified the flesh with its passions and desires.

(Galatians 5:25) 
If we live in the Spirit, let us also walk in the Spirit.

(Galatians 5:26) 
Let us not become conceited, provoking one another, envying one another.

(Galatians 6:1) 
Brothers, if a man is caught in some sin, you who are spiritual should correct him with the spirit of gentleness, being mindful of yourself, lest you also be tempted.

(Galatians 6:2) 
Carry one another's burdens, and in this way you will fulfill the law of Christ.

(Galatians 6:3) 
For if anyone thinks himself to be something when he is nothing, he deceives himself.

(Galatians 6:4) 
But let each one examine his own work, and then he will have his boasting in himself alone, and not in another.

(Galatians 6:5) 
For each one will bear his own burden.

(Galatians 6:6) 
Let the one who is taught in the word share all good things with the one who teaches.

(Galatians 6:7) 
Do not be deceived: God is not mocked. For whatever a man sows, that he will also reap.

(Galatians 6:8) 
For he who sows to his flesh will from the flesh reap corruption; but he who sows to the Spirit will from the Spirit reap eternal life.

(Galatians 6:9) 
And let us not grow weary in doing good, for at the proper time we will reap, if we do not give up.

(Galatians 6:10) 
So then, as we have opportunity, let us do good to all, but especially to those who are of the household of faith.

(Galatians 6:11) 
See with what large letters I have written to you with my own hand.

(Galatians 6:12) 
Those who want to make a good show in the flesh are the ones who try to compel you to be circumcised, simply so that they may not suffer persecution for the cross of Christ.

(Galatians 6:13) 
For even those who are circumcised do not keep the law, but they want you to be circumcised so that they may boast in your flesh.

(Galatians 6:14) 
But may it never be that I should boast except in the cross of our Lord Jesus Christ, by whom the world has been crucified to me, and I to the world.

(Galatians 6:15) 
For in Christ Jesus neither circumcision nor uncircumcision is of any avail, but a new creation.

(Galatians 6:16) 
And as for all who will follow this rule, may peace and mercy be upon them, and upon the Israel of God.

(Galatians 6:17) 
From now on, let no one bother me; for I bear the marks of the Lord Jesus in my body.

(Galatians 6:18) 
The grace of our Lord Jesus Christ be with your spirit, brothers. Amen.

(Ephesians 1:1) 
Paul, a commissioned apostle of Jesus Christ by the will of God, to the holy ones who are at Ephesus, and to the faithful in Christ Jesus.

(Ephesians 1:2) 
Grace to you and peace from God our Father and from the Lord Jesus Christ.

(Ephesians 1:3) 
Blessed be God and the Father of our Lord Jesus Christ, who has blessed us with every spiritual blessing in the universe, in Christ,

(Ephesians 1:4) 
even as He chose us in Him before the beginning of the universe, that we should be holy and without blemish before Him in love,

(Ephesians 1:5) 
who predestined us to be adopted as sons through Jesus Christ to Himself, according to the purpose of His will,

(Ephesians 1:6) 
to the praise of the glory of His grace, with which He has graced us in His beloved Son.

(Ephesians 1:7) 
In Him we have redemption through His blood, the remission of sins according to the riches of His grace,

(Ephesians 1:8) 
which He poured out on us in all wisdom and prudence,

(Ephesians 1:9) 
making known to us the mystery of His will, according to His good pleasure which He purposed in Him,

(Ephesians 1:10) 
to be carried out in the fullness of time: that He would bring all things together in Christ, those in the universe and those on the earth—in Him;

(Ephesians 1:11) 
in whom also we have obtained an inheritance, having been predestined according to the purpose of Him who works all things according to the counsel of His will,

(Ephesians 1:12) 
so that we who first hoped in Christ might be to the praise of His glory.

(Ephesians 1:13) 
In Him, you also, after listening to the word of truth, the Gospel of your salvation—in Him, after you also believed, you were sealed with the Holy Spirit of promise,

(Ephesians 1:14) 
who is the pledge of our inheritance, with a view to the redemption of God's own possession, to the praise of His glory.

(Ephesians 1:15) 
For this reason I also, having heard of the faith in the Lord Jesus which is among you and your love for all the saints,

(Ephesians 1:16) 
do not cease to give thanks for you, while making mention of you in my prayers,

(Ephesians 1:17) 
that the God of our Lord Jesus Christ, the Father of glory, may give you a spirit of wisdom and revelation in the knowledge of Him,

(Ephesians 1:18) 
the eyes of your heart being enlightened, so that you may know what is the hope of His calling, what are the riches of the glory of His inheritance in the saints,

(Ephesians 1:19) 
and what is the surpassing greatness of His power toward us who believe, in accordance with the working of the strength of His might,

(Ephesians 1:20) 
which He brought about in Christ, when He raised Him from the dead and seated Him at His right hand in the universe,

(Ephesians 1:21) 
far above all rule and authority and power and dominion, and every name that is named, not only in this age but also in the one to come.

(Ephesians 1:22) 
And He put all things in subjection under His feet, and gave Him as head over all things to the Church,

(Ephesians 1:23) 
which is His body, the fullness of Him who fills all in all.

(Ephesians 2:1) 
When you were dead, because of your sins and failings,

(Ephesians 2:2) 
you lived according to the ways of the world. You followed the devil, the prince of the power of the air, the evil spirit who now works in those who do not believe,

(Ephesians 2:3) 
Like them, we all once lived in the desires of our flesh, doing what our flesh and minds wanted. We were by nature children of wrath, like everyone else.

(Ephesians 2:4) 
But God, who is rich in mercy, because of his great love for us,

(Ephesians 2:5) 
made us alive with Christ, even when we were dead in sins. God saved you by his grace.

(Ephesians 2:6) 
And God raised us up with Christ and seated us with him in the heavens,

(Ephesians 2:7) 
to show in the ages to come the immeasurable riches of his grace in kindness toward us in Christ Jesus.

(Ephesians 2:8) 
For by grace you have been saved through faith, and this is not your own doing; it is the gift of God,

(Ephesians 2:9) 
not because of works, lest anyone should boast.

(Ephesians 2:10) 
For we are his workmanship, created in Christ Jesus for good works, which God prepared beforehand, that we should walk in them.

(Ephesians 2:11) 
Therefore remember that at one time you Gentiles in the flesh, called “the uncircumcision” by what is called the circumcision, which is done in the flesh by hands,

(Ephesians 2:12) 
were at that time separated from Christ, alienated from the commonwealth of Israel and strangers to the covenants of promise, having no hope and without God in the world.

(Ephesians 2:13) 
But now in Christ Jesus you who once were far off have been brought near by the blood of Christ.

(Ephesians 2:14) 
For he himself is our peace, who has made us both one and has broken down in his flesh the dividing wall of hostility

(Ephesians 2:15) 
by abolishing the law of commandments and ordinances, that he might create in himself one new man in place of the two, so making peace,

(Ephesians 2:16) 
and might reconcile us both to God in one body through the cross, thereby killing the hostility.

(Ephesians 2:17) 
And he came and preached peace to you who were far off and peace to those who were near.

(Ephesians 2:18) 
For through him we both have access in one Spirit to the Father.

(Ephesians 2:19) 
So then you are no longer strangers and aliens, but you are fellow citizens with the saints and members of the household of God,

(Ephesians 2:20) 
built on the foundation of the apostles and prophets, Christ Jesus himself being the cornerstone,

(Ephesians 2:21) 
in whom the whole structure, being joined together, grows into a holy temple in the Lord.

(Ephesians 2:22) 
In him you also are being built together into a dwelling place for God by the Spirit.

(Ephesians 3:1) 
For this cause, I, Paul, the one imprisoned for the sake of Jesus Christ for the sake of you who are not Jews—

(Ephesians 3:2) 
Assuming you’ve heard about the special plan of God’s grace, which was given to me for your sake:

(Ephesians 3:3) 
That by a direct revelation, I have come to understand the mystery of the Church—just as I have written briefly above—

(Ephesians 3:4) 
By reading this, you will see my insight into the mystery of Christ.

(Ephesians 3:5) 
This mystery was not made known to those who lived in past generations, but now it has been revealed to the holy apostles and prophets, through the Holy Spirit:

(Ephesians 3:6) 
That the non-Jews are co-heirs and members of the same body, who share in the promises in Christ Jesus, through the Gospel:

(Ephesians 3:7) 
Of this Gospel, I have become a servant, through the gift of God’s grace, which was given to me through the working of His power.

(Ephesians 3:8) 
This grace was given to me, who is the least of all the saints: that I should announce the good news of Christ’s riches to all the non-Jewish nations.

(Ephesians 3:9) 
And to give understanding of what is the plan of this mystery, which was hidden for all time in God, who created all things.

(Ephesians 3:10) 
The purpose of this is that, now, the principalities and powers in the universe may come to know the many forms of God’s wisdom, through the Church.

(Ephesians 3:11) 
This plan was according to the eternal intention, which He made in Christ Jesus Our Lord:

(Ephesians 3:12) 
In Him we have confidence, and through faith in Him, we are free to approach God.

(Ephesians 3:13) 
So I ask that you do not be discouraged by my sufferings for your sake, which is your glory.

(Ephesians 3:14) 
Because of this, I bow my knees before the Father of Our Lord Jesus Christ,

(Ephesians 3:15) 
From whom all family in the universe, and on the earth, are named.

(Ephesians 3:16) 
May He grant that you, according to the riches of His glory, be strengthened with power through His Spirit in the inner self,

(Ephesians 3:17) 
That Christ may dwell in your hearts through faith; may you be rooted and grounded in love,

(Ephesians 3:18) 
So that you may have the power to comprehend, with all the saints, what is the breadth, and length, and height, and depth—

(Ephesians 3:19) 
To know also the surpassing love of Christ, that you may be filled with all the fullness of God.

(Ephesians 3:20) 
Now to Him who is able to do far more abundantly than all that we ask or think, according to the power at work within us,

(Ephesians 3:21) 
To Him be glory in the Church and in Christ Jesus throughout all generations, forever and ever. Amen.

(Ephesians 4:1) 
So I, a prisoner for the Lord, beg you to live a life worthy of the calling you have received.

(Ephesians 4:2) 
Be humble and gentle, be patient, bearing with one another in love,

(Ephesians 4:3) 
make every effort to keep the unity of the Spirit through the bond of peace.

(Ephesians 4:4) 
There is one body and one Spirit, just as you were called to one hope when you were called,

(Ephesians 4:5) 
one Lord, one faith, one baptism,

(Ephesians 4:6) 
one God and Father of all, who is over all, and through all, and in all.

(Ephesians 4:7) 
But to each one of us grace has been given as Christ apportioned it.

(Ephesians 4:8) 
This is why it says: “When he ascended on high, he took many captives and gave gifts to mankind.”

(Ephesians 4:9) 
(What does “he ascended” mean except that he also descended to the lower, earthly regions?

(Ephesians 4:10) 
He who descended is the very one who ascended higher than all the heavens, in order to fill the whole universe.)

(Ephesians 4:11) 
So Christ himself gave the apostles, the prophets, the evangelists, the pastors and teachers,

(Ephesians 4:12) 
to equip his people for works of service, so that the body of Christ may be built up

(Ephesians 4:13) 
until we all reach unity in the faith and in the knowledge of the Son of God, as we mature to the full measure of the stature of Christ.

(Ephesians 4:14) 
Then we will no longer be infants, tossed back and forth by the waves, and blown here and there by every wind of teaching and by the cunning and craftiness of people in their deceitful scheming.

(Ephesians 4:15) 
Instead, speaking the truth in love, we will grow to become in every respect the mature body of him who is the head, that is, Christ.

(Ephesians 4:16) 
From him the whole body, joined and held together by every supporting ligament, grows and builds itself up in love, as each part does its work.

(Ephesians 4:17) 
So I tell you this, and insist on it in the Lord, that you must no longer live as the Gentiles do, in the futility of their thinking.

(Ephesians 4:18) 
They are darkened in their understanding and separated from the life of God because of the ignorance that is in them due to the hardening of their hearts.

(Ephesians 4:19) 
Having lost all sensitivity, they have given themselves over to sensuality so as to indulge in every kind of impurity, and they are full of greed.

(Ephesians 4:20) 
That, however, is not the way of life you learned

(Ephesians 4:21) 
when you heard about Christ and were taught in him in accordance with the truth that is in Jesus.

(Ephesians 4:22) 
You were taught, with regard to your former way of life, to put off your old self, which is being corrupted by its deceitful desires;

(Ephesians 4:23) 
to be made new in the attitude of your minds;

(Ephesians 4:24) 
and to put on the new self, created to be like God in true righteousness and holiness.

(Ephesians 4:25) 
Therefore each of you must put off falsehood and speak truthfully to your neighbor, for we are all members of one body.

(Ephesians 4:26) 
“In your anger do not sin”: Do not let the sun go down while you are still angry,

(Ephesians 4:27) 
and do not give the devil a foothold.

(Ephesians 4:28) 
Anyone who has been stealing must steal no longer, but must work, doing something useful with their own hands, that they may have something to share with those in need.

(Ephesians 4:29) 
Do not let any unwholesome talk come out of your mouths, but only what is helpful for building others up according to their needs, that it may benefit those who listen.

(Ephesians 4:30) 
And do not grieve the Holy Spirit of God, with whom you were sealed for the day of redemption.

(Ephesians 4:31) 
Get rid of all bitterness, rage and anger, brawling and slander, along with every form of malice.

(Ephesians 4:32) 
Be kind and compassionate to one another, forgiving each other, just as in Christ God forgave you.

(Ephesians 5:1) 
So, become imitators of God, as beloved children.

(Ephesians 5:2) 
And walk in love, just as Christ loved us, and offered Himself for us, an offering and sacrifice to God for a pleasing fragrance.

(Ephesians 5:3) 
But fornication and every impurity or greed, let it not even be named among you, as is fitting for saints.

(Ephesians 5:4) 
Or indecency, or foolish talk, or obscenity, which are not becoming, but rather thanksgiving.

(Ephesians 5:5) 
For know and understand this: that every fornicator or impure person or the greedy, who is a servant of idols, does not have an inheritance in the kingdom of Christ and of God.

(Ephesians 5:6) 
Let no one deceive you with empty words, for because of these things comes the wrath of God upon the sons of disobedience.

(Ephesians 5:7) 
Therefore, do not be partakers with them.

(Ephesians 5:8) 
For you were once darkness, but now you are light in the Lord. Walk as children of light.

(Ephesians 5:9) 
(for the fruit of light is in all goodness and justice and truth),

(Ephesians 5:10) 
proving what is pleasing to God.

(Ephesians 5:11) 
And do not share in the unfruitful works of darkness, but rather reprove them.

(Ephesians 5:12) 
For the things done by them in secret, it is shameful even to speak of.

(Ephesians 5:13) 
But all things that are reproved are made manifest by the light.

(Ephesians 5:14) 
For everything that is made manifest is light.

(Ephesians 5:15) 
Therefore, it says: "Awake, you who sleep, and arise from the dead, and Christ will enlighten you."

(Ephesians 5:16) 
See, therefore, brothers, how carefully you walk: not as unwise,

(Ephesians 5:17) 
but as wise, redeeming the time, because the days are evil.

(Ephesians 5:18) 
Therefore, do not become foolish, but understanding what the will of God is.

(Ephesians 5:19) 
And do not be drunk with wine, in which is debauchery, but be filled with the Holy Spirit,

(Ephesians 5:20) 
speaking to yourselves in psalms and hymns and spiritual songs, singing and making melody in your hearts to the Lord,

(Ephesians 5:21) 
giving thanks always for all things in the name of our Lord Jesus Christ to God and the Father:

(Ephesians 5:22) 
Be subject to one another in the fear of Christ.

(Ephesians 5:23) 
Wives, be subject to your husbands, as to the Lord.

(Ephesians 5:24) 
For the husband is the head of the wife, as Christ is the head of the Church: He is the Savior of His body.

(Ephesians 5:25) 
But as the Church is subject to Christ, so also let wives be to their husbands in all things.

(Ephesians 5:26) 
Husbands, love your wives, just as Christ loved the Church, and gave Himself up for her,

(Ephesians 5:27) 
that He might sanctify her, cleansing her by the washing of water with the word of life,

(Ephesians 5:28) 
that He might present her to Himself a glorious Church, not having spot or wrinkle or any such thing, but that she should be holy and without blemish.

(Ephesians 5:29) 
So also husbands should love their wives as their own bodies. He who loves his wife loves himself.

(Ephesians 5:30) 
For no one ever hated his own flesh: but nourishes and cherishes it, as also Christ does the Church:

(Ephesians 5:31) 
because we are members of His body, of His flesh and of His bones.

(Ephesians 5:32) 
“Therefore a man shall leave his father and his mother and be joined to his wife, and the two shall become one flesh.”

(Ephesians 5:33) 
This is a great mystery, and I mean in Christ and in the Church.

(Ephesians 6:1) 
Children, obey your parents in the Lord; this is right.

(Ephesians 6:2) 
“Honor your father and your mother.” This is the first commandment with a promise:

(Ephesians 6:3) 
“that it may be well with you and that you may live long on the earth.”

(Ephesians 6:4) 
And, you fathers, do not provoke your children to wrath, but bring them up in the discipline and correction of the Lord.

(Ephesians 6:5) 
Slaves, be obedient to those who are your masters according to the flesh, with fear and trembling, in the simplicity of your heart, as to Christ:

(Ephesians 6:6) 
Not serving to the eye, as pleasing men, but as servants of Christ, doing the will of God from the heart,

(Ephesians 6:7) 
Serving with good will as to the Lord, and not to men:

(Ephesians 6:8) 
Knowing that whatever good anyone does, this he will receive from the Lord, whether slave or free.

(Ephesians 6:9) 
And, you masters, do the same things to them, remitting threats, knowing that both theirs and yours is the Lord in heaven, and there is no respect of persons with Him.

(Ephesians 6:10) 
For the rest, be strengthened in the Lord and in the power of His might.

(Ephesians 6:11) 
Put on the armor of God, that you may be able to stand against the deceits of the devil.

(Ephesians 6:12) 
For we are not wrestling against flesh and blood, but against principalities and powers, against the world rulers of this darkness, against the spiritual wickedness in the high places.

(Ephesians 6:13) 
Therefore, take up the armor of God, that you may be able to resist in the evil day and, being perfect in all things, to stand.

(Ephesians 6:14) 
Stand, therefore, having your loins girt about with truth and having put on the breastplate of justice,

(Ephesians 6:15) 
And having your feet shod with the preparation of the gospel of peace:

(Ephesians 6:16) 
In all things, taking up the shield of faith, with which you may be able to extinguish all the fiery darts of the wicked one.

(Ephesians 6:17) 
And take the helmet of salvation and the sword of the Spirit (which is the word of God).

(Ephesians 6:18) 
By every prayer and supplication, praying at all times in the spirit, and in this watching with all insistence and supplication for all the saints:

(Ephesians 6:19) 
And for me, that speech may be given to me, in the opening of my mouth, with confidence to make known the mystery of the gospel:

(Ephesians 6:20) 
For which I am an ambassador in a chain, so that I may dare to speak it, as I ought to speak.

(Ephesians 6:21) 
But that you also may know the things concerning me, and what I am doing, Tychicus, the most beloved brother and a faithful minister in the Lord, will make all things known to you:

(Ephesians 6:22) 
Whom I have sent to you for this very thing, that you may know the things concerning us, and that he may comfort your hearts.

(Ephesians 6:23) 
Peace to the brethren, and love with faith from God the Father and the Lord Jesus Christ.

(Ephesians 6:24) 
Grace with all those who love our Lord Jesus Christ in incorruption. Amen.

(Philippians 1:1) 
Paul and Timothy, servants of Jesus Christ, send greetings to all the holy ones in Christ Jesus who are at Philippi, including their overseers and those who serve them.

(Philippians 1:2) 
May grace and peace be granted to you by God our Father and by the Lord Jesus Christ.

(Philippians 1:3) 
I thank my God whenever I think of you,

(Philippians 1:4) 
always in my every prayer, I pray with joy for all of you,

(Philippians 1:5) 
because you have shared the Gospel from the very first day until now:

(Philippians 1:6) 
I am sure of this: God, who has begun this good work in you, will carry it on to completion until the day of Jesus Christ.

(Philippians 1:7) 
It is right that I should feel this way about all of you, because I hold you in my heart. You share in God’s grace with me, and you are with me in my imprisonment, and in the defense and confirmation of the Gospel.

(Philippians 1:8) 
God is my witness that I long for all of you with the deep love of Jesus Christ.

(Philippians 1:9) 
And I pray that your love may overflow more and more, with knowledge and with all insight,

(Philippians 1:10) 
so that you may discern what is best, and be pure and blameless for the day of Christ,

(Philippians 1:11) 
filled with the fruit of righteousness that comes through Jesus Christ, to the glory and praise of God.

(Philippians 1:12) 
Now I want you to know, brothers and sisters, that what has happened to me has actually served to advance the Gospel,

(Philippians 1:13) 
so that my imprisonment for Christ has become well known throughout the whole praetorian guard and to everyone else.

(Philippians 1:14) 
And because of my imprisonment, most of the brothers and sisters have been encouraged to speak the word of God more courageously and fearlessly.

(Philippians 1:15) 
It is true that some preach Christ out of envy and rivalry, but others out of goodwill.

(Philippians 1:16) 
The latter do so in love, knowing that I am put here for the defense of the Gospel.

(Philippians 1:17) 
The former preach Christ out of selfish ambition, not sincerely, supposing that they can add to my distress in my chains.

(Philippians 1:18) 
So what? The important thing is that in every way, whether from wrong motives or true, Christ is preached. And because of this I rejoice. Yes, and I will continue to rejoice,

(Philippians 1:19) 
for I know that through your prayers and God’s provision of the Spirit of Jesus Christ, what has happened to me will turn out for my deliverance.

(Philippians 1:20) 
I eagerly expect and hope that I will in no way be ashamed, but will have sufficient courage so that now as always Christ will be exalted in my body, whether by life or by death.

(Philippians 1:21) 
For to me, to live is Christ and to die is gain.

(Philippians 1:22) 
If I am to go on living in the body, this will mean fruitful labor for me. Yet what shall I choose? I do not know!

(Philippians 1:23) 
I am torn between the two: I desire to depart and be with Christ, which is better by far;

(Philippians 1:24) 
but it is more necessary for you that I remain in the body.

(Philippians 1:25) 
Convinced of this, I know that I will remain and will continue with all of you for your progress and joy in the faith,

(Philippians 1:26) 
so that through my being with you again, your boasting in Christ Jesus will abound on account of me.

(Philippians 1:27) 
Whatever happens, conduct yourselves in a manner worthy of the Gospel of Christ. Then, whether I come and see you or only hear about you in my absence, I will know that you stand firm in one spirit, striving together as one for the faith of the Gospel,

(Philippians 1:28) 
without being frightened in any way by those who oppose you. This is a sign to them that they will be lost, but that you will be saved—and that by God.

(Philippians 1:29) 
For it has been granted to you on behalf of Christ not only to believe in him, but also to suffer for him,

(Philippians 1:30) 
since you are going through the same struggle you saw I had, and now hear that I still have.

(Philippians 2:1) 
If therefore there is any consolation in the Son, if any comfort of love, if any fellowship of the Spirit, if any affection and compassion:

(Philippians 2:2) 
Then complete my joy, by having the same understanding, having the same charity, being of one mind, thinking the same thing:

(Philippians 2:3) 
Let nothing be done through contention, nor by empty glory: but in humility of mind, let each esteem others better than themselves:

(Philippians 2:4) 
Not considering each the things that are his own, but the things that are of others.

(Philippians 2:5) 
For let this mind be in you, which was also in Christ Jesus:

(Philippians 2:6) 
Who, being in the form of God, thought it not robbery to be equal to God:

(Philippians 2:7) 
But emptied himself, taking the form of a servant, being made in the likeness of men, and in habit found as a man.

(Philippians 2:8) 
He humbled himself, becoming obedient unto death, even the death of the cross.

(Philippians 2:9) 
For which cause also God hath exalted him, and hath given him a name which is above all names:

(Philippians 2:10) 
That in the name of Jesus every knee should bow, of those that are in heaven, on earth, and under the earth:

(Philippians 2:11) 
And that every tongue should confess that the Lord Jesus Christ is in the glory of God the Father.

(Philippians 2:12) 
Wherefore, my dearly beloved, as you have always obeyed, not as in my presence only, but much more now in my absence, with fear and trembling work out your salvation.

(Philippians 2:13) 
For it is God who worketh in you both to will and to accomplish, according to his good will.

(Philippians 2:14) 
Do all things without murmurings and hesitations:

(Philippians 2:15) 
That you may be blameless and harmless, children of God without reproach, in the midst of a depraved and perverse nation: among whom you shine as lights in the world,

(Philippians 2:16) 
Holding fast the word of life: that I may glory in the day of Christ, that I have not run in vain, nor labored in vain.

(Philippians 2:17) 
But if I am to be sacrificed upon the sacrifice and service of your faith, I rejoice, and congratulate with you all.

(Philippians 2:18) 
And for the same things do you also rejoice, and congratulate with me.

(Philippians 2:19) 
But I hope in the Lord Jesus to send Timothy to you shortly, that I also may be of good comfort, when I know the things concerning you.

(Philippians 2:20) 
For I have no one so of one mind, who with sincere care for you, will care about the things that are of Jesus Christ.

(Philippians 2:21) 
For all seek the things that are their own, not the things that are of Jesus Christ.

(Philippians 2:22) 
But know ye the proof of him, that as a son with the father, he hath served with me in the gospel.

(Philippians 2:23) 
Him therefore I hope to send immediately, as soon as I shall see what shall be about me.

(Philippians 2:24) 
And I trust in the Lord that I myself also shall come to you shortly.

(Philippians 2:25) 
But I have thought it necessary to send to you Epaphroditus, my brother and fellow worker and fellow soldier, but your apostle and the minister of my need.

(Philippians 2:26) 
Because indeed he longed for you all, and was sad, for that you had heard that he was sick.

(Philippians 2:27) 
For indeed he was sick, even unto death; but God had mercy on him: and not on him only, but on me also, that I might not have sorrow upon sorrow.

(Philippians 2:28) 
I sent him therefore the more diligently, that, seeing him again, you may rejoice, and I may be the less sorrowful.

(Philippians 2:29) 
Receive him therefore with all joy in the Lord; and such as these hold in honor:

(Philippians 2:30) 
Because for the work of Christ he came to the point of death, delivering his life, that he might fulfill that which was wanting of your service towards me.

(Philippians 3:1) 
Finally, my brothers, rejoice in the Lord! It is no trouble for me to write the same things to you, and it is a safeguard for you.

(Philippians 3:2) 
Watch out for the dogs! Beware of evil workers! Beware of those who mutilate the flesh.

(Philippians 3:3) 
For we are the circumcision, we who worship God in the Spirit, who rejoice in Christ Jesus, and who put no confidence in the flesh

(Philippians 3:4) 
Though I myself have reason for confidence in the flesh also. If anyone else thinks he has reason for confidence in the flesh, I have more:

(Philippians 3:5) 
circumcised on the eighth day, of the people of Israel, of the tribe of Benjamin, a Hebrew of Hebrews; in regard to the law, a Pharisee;

(Philippians 3:6) 
as for zeal, persecuting the Church; as for legal righteousness, faultless.

(Philippians 3:7) 
But whatever gain I had, I counted as loss for the sake of Christ.

(Philippians 3:8) 
Indeed, I count everything as loss because of the surpassing worth of knowing Christ Jesus my Lord. For his sake I have suffered the loss of all things and count them as rubbish, in order that I may gain Christ

(Philippians 3:9) 
and be found in him, not having a righteousness of my own that comes from the law, but that which comes through faith in Christ, the righteousness from God that depends on faith

(Philippians 3:10) 
that I may know him and the power of his resurrection, and may share his sufferings, becoming like him in his death,

(Philippians 3:11) 
that by any means possible I may attain the resurrection from the dead.

(Philippians 3:12) 
Not that I have already obtained this or am already perfect, but I press on to make it my own, because Christ Jesus has made me his own.

(Philippians 3:13) 
Brothers, I do not consider that I have made it my own. But one thing I do: forgetting what lies behind and straining forward to what lies ahead,

(Philippians 3:14) 
I press on toward the goal for the prize of the upward call of God in Christ Jesus.

(Philippians 3:15) 
Let those of us who are mature think this way, and if in anything you think otherwise, God will reveal this also to you.

(Philippians 3:16) 
Only let us hold true to what we have attained.

(Philippians 3:17) 
Brothers, join in imitating me, and keep your eyes on those who walk according to the example you have in us.

(Philippians 3:18) 
For many, of whom I have often told you and now tell you even with tears, walk as enemies of the cross of Christ.

(Philippians 3:19) 
Their end is destruction, their god is their belly, and their glory is in their shame, who set their minds on earthly things.

(Philippians 3:20) 
But our citizenship is in heaven, and from it we await a Savior, the Lord Jesus Christ,

(Philippians 3:21) 
who will transform our lowly body to be like his glorious body, by the power that enables him even to subject all things to himself.

(Philippians 4:1) 
So, my beloved brothers and sisters, whom I love and long to see, you who are my joy and crown, stand firm in the Lord, my dear ones.

(Philippians 4:2) 
I urge Euodia and I plead with Syntyche to agree in the Lord.

(Philippians 4:3) 
And I ask you also, my loyal companion, help these women, for they worked with me in the Gospel, along with Clement and the rest of my fellow workers, whose names are in the book of life.

(Philippians 4:4) 
Rejoice in the Lord always; again, I say, rejoice.

(Philippians 4:5) 
Let your gentleness be known to all men. The Lord is near.

(Philippians 4:6) 
Have no anxiety about anything; but in everything, by prayer and supplication, with thanksgiving, let your requests be made known to God.

(Philippians 4:7) 
And the peace of God, which surpasses all understanding, will guard your hearts and your minds in Christ Jesus.

(Philippians 4:8) 
Finally, brothers and sisters, whatever is true, whatever is honorable, whatever is just, whatever is pure, whatever is lovely, whatever is commendable, if there is any excellence, if there is anything worthy of praise, think about these things.

(Philippians 4:9) 
The things which you have learned and received and heard and seen in me, these do: and the God of peace will be with you.

(Philippians 4:10) 
I rejoiced in the Lord greatly that now at last you have revived your concern for me; though you were concerned before, you lacked an opportunity.

(Philippians 4:11) 
Not that I speak in regard to need; for I have learned, in whatever state I am, to be content.

(Philippians 4:12) 
I know how to be brought low, and I know how to abound. In any and all circumstances I have learned the secret of facing plenty and hunger, abundance and need.

(Philippians 4:13) 
I can do all things through him who strengthens me.

(Philippians 4:14) 
Yet it was kind of you to share in my trouble.

(Philippians 4:15) 
And you Philippians yourselves know that in the beginning of the Gospel, when I departed from Macedonia, no church shared with me in the matter of giving and receiving except you only.

(Philippians 4:16) 
For even in Thessalonica you sent me help more than once when I was in need.

(Philippians 4:17) 
Not that I seek the gift, but I seek the fruit that increases to your credit.

(Philippians 4:18) 
I have received everything in full and have an abundance; I am filled, having received from Epaphroditus the things that you sent, a fragrant offering, a sacrifice acceptable and pleasing to God.

(Philippians 4:19) 
My God will supply every need of yours according to his riches in glory in Christ Jesus.

(Philippians 4:20) 
To our God and Father be glory for ever and ever. Amen.

(Philippians 4:21) 
Greet every saint in Christ Jesus. The brothers and sisters who are with me greet you.

(Philippians 4:22) 
All the saints greet you, especially those of Caesar’s household.

(Philippians 4:23) 
The grace of our Lord Jesus Christ be with your spirit. Amen.

(Colossians 1:1) 
Paul, sent on a mission by the will of God, along with our brother Timothy,

(Colossians 1:2) 
to the faithful brothers and sisters in Christ living in Colossae. May grace and peace come to you from God our Father and from our Lord Jesus Christ.

(Colossians 1:3) 
We always thank God, the Father of our Lord Jesus Christ, when we pray for you,

(Colossians 1:4) 
because we have heard of your faith in Christ Jesus and your love for all the saints,

(Colossians 1:5) 
which is founded on the hope you have in the universe. You learned about this hope through the message of the Gospel, which is the truth,

(Colossians 1:6) 
the same Gospel that has come to you and is bearing fruit and growing throughout the whole world, just as it has been doing among you since the day you heard it and understood God’s grace in all its truth.

(Colossians 1:7) 
You learned this from Epaphras, our dear fellow servant, who is a faithful minister of Christ on your behalf,

(Colossians 1:8) 
and who also told us about your love in the Spirit.

(Colossians 1:9) 
For this reason, since the day we heard about you, we have not stopped praying for you. We continually ask God that you may be filled with the knowledge of His will through all the wisdom and understanding that the Spirit gives,

(Colossians 1:10) 
so that you may live a life worthy of the Lord and please Him in every way, bearing fruit in every good work, growing in the knowledge of God,

(Colossians 1:11) 
being strengthened with all power according to His glorious might so that you may have great endurance and patience,

(Colossians 1:12) 
and giving joyful thanks to the Father, who has qualified you to share in the inheritance of the saints in the light.

(Colossians 1:13) 
For He has rescued us from the dominion of darkness and brought us into the kingdom of the Son He loves,

(Colossians 1:14) 
in whom we have redemption, the forgiveness of sins.

(Colossians 1:15) 
The Son is the image of the invisible God, the firstborn over all creation,

(Colossians 1:16) 
For in him all things were created: things in heaven and on earth, visible and invisible, whether thrones or powers or rulers or authorities; all things have been created through him and for him.

(Colossians 1:17) 
He is before all things, and in him all things hold together.

(Colossians 1:18) 
And he is the head of the body, the Church; he is the beginning and the firstborn from among the dead, so that in everything he might have the supremacy.

(Colossians 1:19) 
For God was pleased to have all his fullness dwell in him,

(Colossians 1:20) 
and through him to reconcile to himself all things, whether things on earth or things in heaven, by making peace through his blood, shed on the cross.

(Colossians 1:21) 
Once you were alienated from God and were enemies in your minds because of your evil behavior.

(Colossians 1:22) 
But now he has reconciled you by Christ’s physical body through death to present you holy in his sight, without blemish and free from accusation.

(Colossians 1:23) 
If you continue in your faith, established and firm, and do not move from the hope held out in the gospel. This is the gospel that you heard and that has been proclaimed to every creature under heaven, and of which I, Paul, have become a servant.

(Colossians 1:24) 
Now I rejoice in what I am suffering for you, and I fill up in my flesh what is still lacking in regard to Christ’s afflictions, for the sake of his body, which is the church,

(Colossians 1:25) 
I have become its servant, according to God’s commission that was given to me for you, to present to you the word of God in its fullness.

(Colossians 1:26) 
This mystery, which has been kept hidden for ages and generations, but is now disclosed to the Lord’s holy people.

(Colossians 1:27) 
To them God has chosen to make known among the Gentiles the glorious riches of this mystery, which is Christ in you, the hope of glory.

(Colossians 1:28) 
We proclaim him, warning and teaching everyone with all wisdom, so that we may present everyone fully mature in Christ.

(Colossians 1:29) 
To this end I strenuously contend with all the energy Christ so powerfully works in me.

(Colossians 2:1) 
I want you to know how much I struggle for you, for those in Laodicea, and for everyone who has never seen my face in person.

(Colossians 2:2) 
I want them to be encouraged and united by love, enriched with a full understanding, and with the knowledge of the mystery of God the Father, and of Christ.

(Colossians 2:3) 
In Christ are hidden all the treasures of wisdom and knowledge.

(Colossians 2:4) 
I say this so that no one will deceive you with smooth words.

(Colossians 2:5) 
Though I am absent in body, I am with you in spirit. I am glad to see your order and the strength of your faith in Christ.

(Colossians 2:6) 
Therefore, since you have received Christ Jesus the Lord, walk in him.

(Colossians 2:7) 
Be rooted and built up in him, and strengthened in the faith as you were taught, overflowing with thankfulness.

(Colossians 2:8) 
Be careful that no one deceives you with philosophy, empty deceit, the tradition of men, the elemental spirits of the world, and not according to Christ.

(Colossians 2:9) 
For in Christ lives all the fullness of the Godhead bodily.

(Colossians 2:10) 
And you have been filled in him, who is the head of all principality and power.

(Colossians 2:11) 
In him you were also circumcised, but not with a circumcision done by human hands; you were set free from the sinful nature of the body, by the circumcision of Christ.

(Colossians 2:12) 
You were buried with him in baptism, in which you were also raised with him through faith in the power of God, who raised him from the dead.

(Colossians 2:13) 
And you, who were dead in your trespasses and the uncircumcision of your flesh, God made alive together with him, having forgiven us all our trespasses,

(Colossians 2:14) 
blotting out the written code of the decrees that was against us, which was contrary to us; he took it out of the way, nailing it to the cross.

(Colossians 2:15) 
He disarmed the rulers and authorities and put them to open shame, by triumphing over them in him.

(Colossians 2:16) 
Therefore, do not let anyone judge you in respect to food or drink or in respect to a festival, a new moon, or a Sabbath.

(Colossians 2:17) 
These are a shadow of the things to come, but the substance belongs to Christ.

(Colossians 2:18) 
Do not let anyone defraud you of your prize by insisting on self-abasement and the worship of angels, dwelling on things that he has not seen, puffed up without cause by his sensuous mind,

(Colossians 2:19) 
and not holding fast to the head, from whom the whole body, nourished and knit together through its joints and ligaments, grows with a growth that is from God.

(Colossians 2:20) 
If with Christ you died to the elemental spirits of the world, why, as though you were still living in the world, do you submit to regulations—

(Colossians 2:21) 
“Do not handle,” “Do not taste,” “Do not touch”

(Colossians 2:22) 
(which all are destined to perish with use)—according to human precepts and teachings?

(Colossians 2:23) 
These have indeed an appearance of wisdom in promoting self-imposed piety, humility, and severity to the body, but they are of no value in checking the indulgence of the flesh.

(Colossians 3:1) 
Since you are resurrected with Christ, you should seek the things that are above, where Christ is seated at the right hand of God:

(Colossians 3:2) 
You should focus on the things above, not the things of the earth.

(Colossians 3:3) 
For you have died, and your life is hidden with Christ in God.

(Colossians 3:4) 
When Christ, who is your life, appears, then you also will appear with Him in glory.

(Colossians 3:5) 
Therefore, you must put to death the members of your body that are on the earth: sexual immorality, impurity, lust, evil desire, and greed, which is the worship of idols.

(Colossians 3:6) 
Because of these things, the wrath of God is coming upon those who do not believe.

(Colossians 3:7) 
In these things, you too once walked, when you lived among them.

(Colossians 3:8) 
But now, you must rid yourselves of all these things: anger, wrath, malice, blasphemy, and foul language from your mouth.

(Colossians 3:9) 
Do not lie to each other, stripping off the old self with its practices,

(Colossians 3:10) 
and putting on the new self, which is being renewed in knowledge according to the image of its Creator,

(Colossians 3:11) 
where there is no Gentile or Jew, circumcision or uncircumcision, barbarian or Scythian, slave or free, but Christ is all and in all.

(Colossians 3:12) 
Therefore, as the chosen ones of God, holy and beloved, clothe yourselves with compassion, kindness, humility, gentleness, and patience,

(Colossians 3:13) 
bearing with one another and forgiving one another, if anyone has a complaint against another; as the Lord has forgiven you, so also you must forgive.

(Colossians 3:14) 
Above all these things, have love, which binds everything together in perfect harmony.

(Colossians 3:15) 
And let the peace of Christ rule in your hearts, to which also you were called in one body; and be thankful.

(Colossians 3:16) 
Let the word of Christ dwell in you richly, teaching and admonishing one another in all wisdom, singing psalms, hymns, and spiritual songs, with thankfulness in your hearts to God.

(Colossians 3:17) 
And whatever you do, in word or deed, do everything in the name of the Lord Jesus, giving thanks to God the Father through Him.

(Colossians 3:18) 
Wives, be subject to your husbands, as is fitting in the Lord.

(Colossians 3:19) 
Husbands, love your wives and do not be harsh with them.

(Colossians 3:20) 
Children, obey your parents in everything, for this is pleasing to the Lord.

(Colossians 3:21) 
Fathers, do not provoke your children to anger, so they do not become discouraged.

(Colossians 3:22) 
Slaves, obey your earthly masters in everything, not only while they are watching, as people-pleasers, but with sincerity of heart, fearing the Lord.

(Colossians 3:23) 
Whatever you do, do it with all your heart, as working for the Lord, not for men,

(Colossians 3:24) 
knowing that from the Lord you will receive the inheritance as your reward. You are serving the Lord Christ.

(Colossians 3:25) 
For the wrongdoer will be paid back for his wrongs, and there is no partiality.

(Colossians 4:1) 
Masters, give to your servants what is just and fair, knowing that you also have a Master in the universe.

(Colossians 4:2) 
Be persistent in prayer, being watchful in it with thanksgiving.

(Colossians 4:3) 
Pray also for us, that God may open to us a door for the word, to speak the mystery of Christ (for which also I am bound),

(Colossians 4:4) 
that I may make it manifest, as I ought to speak.

(Colossians 4:5) 
Walk with wisdom toward those who are outside, redeeming the time.

(Colossians 4:6) 
Let your speech always be in grace, seasoned with salt: so that you may know how you ought to answer each person.

(Colossians 4:7) 
All that concerns me, and what I do, Tychicus, the most dear brother, and faithful minister, and fellow servant in the Lord, will make known to you:

(Colossians 4:8) 
whom I have sent to you for this very thing, that you may know the things concerning us, and that he may comfort your hearts,

(Colossians 4:9) 
with Onesimus, a faithful and most dear brother, who is one of you. They will make known to you all things that are done here.

(Colossians 4:10) 
Aristarchus, my fellow prisoner, salutes you; and Mark, the cousin of Barnabas, about whom you have received commands: if he comes to you, receive him:

(Colossians 4:11) 
and Jesus, who is called Justus: who are of the circumcision. These alone are fellow workers for the kingdom of God, who have been a comfort to me.

(Colossians 4:12) 
Epaphras, who is one of you, the servant of Christ Jesus, salutes you, always solicitous for you in prayers, that you may stand perfect and full in all the will of God.

(Colossians 4:13) 
For I bear him witness that he has much labor for you, and for those who are at Laodicea, and for those who are at Hierapolis.

(Colossians 4:14) 
Luke, the most dear physician, salutes you, and Demas.

(Colossians 4:15) 
Salute the brothers who are at Laodicea, and Nymphas, and the church that is in his house.

(Colossians 4:16) 
And when this letter has been read among you, cause that it be read also in the church of the Laodiceans: and that which is [sent] from Laodicea, read that also among yourselves.

(Colossians 4:17) 
And say to Archippus, “Take heed to the ministry which you have received in the Lord, that you fulfill it.”

(Colossians 4:18) 
The greeting by the hand of Paul. Be mindful of my bonds. Grace be with you. Amen.

(1 Thessalonians 1:1) 
From Paul, and Silvanus, and Timothy: to the church of the Thessalonians, who are united to God the Father and our Lord Jesus Christ.

(1 Thessalonians 1:2) 
Grace to you, and peace. We give thanks to God always for you all, making mention of you in our prayers without ceasing,

(1 Thessalonians 1:3) 
constantly remembering your work of faith and your labor, and the love and patience of the hope of our Lord Jesus Christ, before God our Father:

(1 Thessalonians 1:4) 
Knowing, brethren beloved by God, your election:

(1 Thessalonians 1:5) 
Because our Gospel came to you not only in word, but also in power, and in the Holy Spirit, and in much fullness, just as you know what kind of men we were among you, for your sakes.

(1 Thessalonians 1:6) 
And you became imitators of us and of the Lord, receiving the word with much tribulation, with the joy of the Holy Spirit,

(1 Thessalonians 1:7) 
so that you were made a pattern to all those who believe, in Macedonia and in Achaia.

(1 Thessalonians 1:8) 
For from you has gone forth the word of the Lord, not only in Macedonia and Achaia, but in every place your faith, which is toward God, has gone forth, so that we need not to speak anything.

(1 Thessalonians 1:9) 
For they themselves relate of us what kind of entrance we had to you: and how you turned to God from idols, to serve the living and true God,

(1 Thessalonians 1:10) 
and to await His Son from the universe—Jesus—whom He raised from the dead, who has delivered us from the wrath to come.

(1 Thessalonians 2:1) 
You know yourselves, brothers, that we didn’t come to you in vain, wasting time or energy:

(1 Thessalonians 2:2) 
But after suffering and enduring insults, as you know, in Philippi, we had the courage given to us by God to preach to you in difficult times.

(1 Thessalonians 2:3) 
For our encouragement did not come from error, nor from uncleanness, nor from trickery:

(1 Thessalonians 2:4) 
but as we were proven worthy by God, that the Gospel be entrusted to us, so do we speak, not as those pleasing men, but God, who knows our hearts.

(1 Thessalonians 2:5) 
For at no time were we in speech with flattery, as you know: nor with an occasion for greed: God is witness.

(1 Thessalonians 2:6) 
Nor seeking glory from men, neither from you, nor from others:

(1 Thessalonians 2:7) 
though we could have been a burden to you, in order to seek the glory of Christ:

(1 Thessalonians 2:8) 
but we became little ones among you, as a mother would nurture her children:

(1 Thessalonians 2:9) 
in this way, we longed for you, and eagerly wished to hand over to you not only the Gospel of God, but also our souls: because you have become very dear to us.

(1 Thessalonians 2:10) 
For you remember, brothers, our labor and toil: for working night and day, so that we might not burden any of you, we preached to you the Gospel of God.

(1 Thessalonians 2:11) 
You are witnesses, and God is too: how holy, just, and blameless we were among you who believed:

(1 Thessalonians 2:12) 
as you know, how we exhorted each of you, as a father does his children,

(1 Thessalonians 2:13) 
assuring, consoling, and testifying to you, that you should walk worthy of God, who has called you to His kingdom and glory.

(1 Thessalonians 2:14) 
For this reason, we also thank God without ceasing: because when you received from us the word of the hearing of God, you received it not as the word of men, but as it truly is the word of God, which works in you who believe.

(1 Thessalonians 2:15) 
For you have become imitators, brothers, of the churches of God which are in Judea in Christ Jesus: because the same things that they suffered were also suffered by you from your own countrymen, as they did from the Jews,

(1 Thessalonians 2:16) 
who also killed the Lord Jesus and the prophets, and persecuted us, and do not please God, and are against all men,

(1 Thessalonians 2:17) 
forbidding us to speak to the Gentiles, so that they may be saved, so that they may always fill up their sins: for the wrath of God has come upon them to the end.

(1 Thessalonians 2:18) 
But we, brothers, being left desolate from you for a time, in appearance, not in heart, we eagerly sought all the more to see your face with great desire.

(1 Thessalonians 2:19) 
Because we wanted to come to you, I, indeed, Paul, once and again: and Satan prevented us.

(1 Thessalonians 2:20) 
For who is our hope, or joy, or the crown of glory? Are you not? Before our Lord Jesus at His coming?

(1 Thessalonians 2:21) 
For you are our glory and joy.

(1 Thessalonians 3:1) 
Because of this, we could not bear to remain alone in Athens.

(1 Thessalonians 3:2) 
So we sent our brother Timothy, a servant of God in the Gospel of Christ, to strengthen you and to exhort you in your faith.

(1 Thessalonians 3:3) 
We sent him so that no one would be shaken by these tribulations. For you yourselves know that we are appointed to this.

(1 Thessalonians 3:4) 
For when we were with you, we told you beforehand that we would suffer tribulation, even as it came to pass, and as you know.

(1 Thessalonians 3:5) 
For this cause, I also, not bearing it any longer, sent to know your faith, lest perhaps the tempter has tempted you and our labor become vain.

(1 Thessalonians 3:6) 
But now, Timothy has come to us from you and brought us good news about your faith and your charity and that you have a good memory of us always, desiring to see us, just as we also want to see you.

(1 Thessalonians 3:7) 
Therefore, brothers, we have been comforted about you in all our necessity and tribulation, through your faith.

(1 Thessalonians 3:8) 
Because now we live, if you stand firm in the Lord.

(1 Thessalonians 3:9) 
For what thanksgiving can we render to God for you, for all the joy wherewith we rejoice for your sakes before God,

(1 Thessalonians 3:10) 
night and day praying more abundantly that we may see your face and may accomplish those things that are wanting to your faith?

(1 Thessalonians 3:11) 
Now God Himself and our Father, and our Lord Jesus Christ, direct our way unto you.

(1 Thessalonians 3:12) 
And may the Lord make you increase and abound in love towards one another and towards all men, even as we do towards you.

(1 Thessalonians 3:13) 
So that he may establish your hearts without blame, in holiness before God and our Father, at the coming of our Lord Jesus Christ with all his saints.

(1 Thessalonians 4:1) 
And now, brothers, we beg you and beseech you in the Lord Jesus Christ, and it is our earnest desire that you continue living the holy life that we have taught you, the life that is pleasing to God, and that you do it even more and more.

(1 Thessalonians 4:2) 
For you know very well what instructions we gave you through the Lord Jesus.

(1 Thessalonians 4:3) 
For this is the will of God, your sanctification: that you stay away from all sexual sin,

(1 Thessalonians 4:4) 
that each of you knows how to control his own body in holiness and honor,

(1 Thessalonians 4:5) 
and not in the lust of passion, as the Gentiles who do not know God do:

(1 Thessalonians 4:6) 
that no one transgress and wrong his brother in this matter. For the Lord is the avenger of all these things, as we have told you and testified before.

(1 Thessalonians 4:7) 
For God has not called us to impurity, but to holiness.

(1 Thessalonians 4:8) 
Therefore, he who rejects this, rejects not man, but God, who has also given His Holy Spirit to you.

(1 Thessalonians 4:9) 
Now concerning fraternal love, we do not need to write to you. For you yourselves have been taught by God to love one another.

(1 Thessalonians 4:10) 
For indeed you do this toward all the brothers who are in all of Macedonia. But we urge you, brothers, to increase more and more,

(1 Thessalonians 4:11) 
and to strive to be at peace, and to mind your own business, and to work with your own hands, as we have commanded you,

(1 Thessalonians 4:12) 
so that you may walk honestly toward those who are outside, and that you may not lack anything.

(1 Thessalonians 4:13) 
But we do not want you to be ignorant, brothers, concerning those who have fallen asleep, so that you do not grieve as the others do who have no hope.

(1 Thessalonians 4:14) 
For if we believe that Jesus died and rose again, even so God will bring with Him those who have fallen asleep through Jesus.

(1 Thessalonians 4:15) 
For this we tell you by the word of the Lord: that we who are alive and remain until the coming of the Lord will not precede those who have fallen asleep.

(1 Thessalonians 4:16) 
For the Lord Himself, with a command, with the voice of the archangel and with the trumpet of God, will descend from the sky: and the dead who are in Christ will rise first.

(1 Thessalonians 4:17) 
Then we who are alive and remain will be caught up together with them in the clouds to meet Christ in the air: and so we will always be with the Lord.

(1 Thessalonians 4:18) 
Therefore, comfort one another with these words.

(1 Thessalonians 5:1) 
Now concerning the times and moments, brothers and sisters, there is no need to write to you about it.

(1 Thessalonians 5:2) 
For you yourselves know perfectly well that the day of the Lord will come like a thief in the night.

(1 Thessalonians 5:3) 
When they say “Peace and safety,” then sudden destruction will come upon them, as labor pains come upon a woman giving birth, and they will not escape.

(1 Thessalonians 5:4) 
But you, brothers and sisters, are not in darkness, that this day should overtake you as a thief.

(1 Thessalonians 5:5) 
For you are all children of light and children of the day; we are not of the night nor of darkness.

(1 Thessalonians 5:6) 
Therefore let us not sleep, as the rest do, but let us keep awake and be sober.

(1 Thessalonians 5:7) 
For those who sleep, sleep at night, and those who get drunk are drunk at night.

(1 Thessalonians 5:8) 
But since we belong to the day, let us be sober, putting on the breastplate of faith and love, and the helmet of the hope of salvation.

(1 Thessalonians 5:9) 
For God has not destined us for wrath, but to obtain salvation through our Lord Jesus Christ,

(1 Thessalonians 5:10) 
who died for us, so that whether we are awake or asleep, we may live together with him.

(1 Thessalonians 5:11) 
Therefore encourage one another and build one another up, as indeed you are doing.

(1 Thessalonians 5:12) 
We ask you, brothers and sisters, to respect those who labor among you and are over you in the Lord and admonish you,

(1 Thessalonians 5:13) 
and to esteem them very highly in love because of their work. Be at peace among yourselves.

(1 Thessalonians 5:14) 
And we exhort you, brothers and sisters, admonish the idle, encourage the fainthearted, help the weak, be patient with all.

(1 Thessalonians 5:15) 
See that no one repays evil for evil to anyone, but always pursue what is good, both for yourselves and for all.

(1 Thessalonians 5:16) 
Rejoice always.

(1 Thessalonians 5:17) 
Pray without ceasing.

(1 Thessalonians 5:18) 
In everything give thanks; for this is God’s will for you in Christ Jesus.

(1 Thessalonians 5:19) 
Do not quench the Spirit.

(1 Thessalonians 5:20) 
Do not despise prophecies,

(1 Thessalonians 5:21) 
but test everything; hold fast to what is good.

(1 Thessalonians 5:22) 
Abstain from every form of evil.

(1 Thessalonians 5:23) 
May the God of peace himself sanctify you completely; and may your spirit and soul and body be kept sound and blameless at the coming of our Lord Jesus Christ.

(1 Thessalonians 5:24) 
He who calls you is faithful; he will surely do it.

(1 Thessalonians 5:25) 
Brothers and sisters, pray for us.

(1 Thessalonians 5:26) 
Greet all the brothers and sisters with a holy kiss.

(1 Thessalonians 5:27) 
I adjure you by the Lord to have this letter read to all the holy brothers and sisters.

(1 Thessalonians 5:28) 
The grace of our Lord Jesus Christ be with you. Amen.

(2 Thessalonians 1:1) 
From Paul, Silas, and Timothy, to the Church of the Thessalonians, who are in God our Father, and in Our Lord Jesus Christ:

(2 Thessalonians 1:2) 
May grace and peace be given to you from God our Father, and from Our Lord Jesus Christ.

(2 Thessalonians 1:3) 
We ought to always give thanks to God for you, brothers, as is proper, because your faith increases so much, and the charity of each one of you abounds toward one another:

(2 Thessalonians 1:4) 
so that we ourselves may glory in you in the churches of God, because of your patience and faith in all your persecutions, and in the tribulations that you endure,

(2 Thessalonians 1:5) 
This is proof of God’s just judgment, that you may be worthy of the Kingdom of God, for which you also suffer:

(2 Thessalonians 1:6) 
Because it is just for God to repay with tribulation those who afflict you:

(2 Thessalonians 1:7) 
and to give rest to you who are afflicted, along with us, at the revelation of Our Lord Jesus Christ with the angels of His power,

(2 Thessalonians 1:8) 
in flaming fire, taking vengeance on those who do not know God, and who do not obey the Gospel of Our Lord Jesus Christ:

(2 Thessalonians 1:9) 
These people will pay the penalty of eternal destruction, away from the presence of the Lord, and from the glory of His power:

(2 Thessalonians 1:10) 
On that day, He will come to be glorified among His holy ones, and to be admired among all who have believed (because our testimony among you was believed).

(2 Thessalonians 1:11) 
Therefore, we always pray for you: that God may deem you worthy of His calling, and may fulfill every desire of goodness, and the work of faith in power,

(2 Thessalonians 1:12) 
so that the name of Our Lord Jesus Christ may be glorified in you, and you in Him, according to the grace of our God, and Our Lord Jesus Christ.

(2 Thessalonians 2:1) 
Now, brothers, we beg you about the second coming of our Lord Jesus Christ, and our gathering to Him.

(2 Thessalonians 2:2) 
Don't let anyone easily shake your faith, nor should you be frightened, whether by a spirit, or by a word, or by a letter as if sent by us, that the Day of the Lord is present.

(2 Thessalonians 2:3) 
Let no one deceive you in any way. Because the Day of the Lord will not come unless the apostasy has come first, and the man of sin, the son of perdition, has been revealed,

(2 Thessalonians 2:4) 
Who opposes and elevates himself above all that is called God, or that is worshiped. This man will sit in the temple of God, showing himself as if he is God.

(2 Thessalonians 2:5) 
Don't you remember that I told you these things when I was still with you?

(2 Thessalonians 2:6) 
Now you know what restrains him, so that he may be revealed in his time.

(2 Thessalonians 2:7) 
For the mystery of iniquity is already at work, only until he who now restrains is taken out of the way.

(2 Thessalonians 2:8) 
And then the lawless one will be revealed, whom the Lord Jesus will kill with the breath of His mouth, and will destroy with the brightness of His coming.

(2 Thessalonians 2:9) 
This man's coming is according to the working of Satan, in all power, and signs, and wonders of lies,

(2 Thessalonians 2:10) 
and in all the deceits of wickedness for those who perish, because they didn't accept the love of the truth, that they might be saved.

(2 Thessalonians 2:11) 
And therefore God will send them the operation of error, that they should believe a lie:

(2 Thessalonians 2:12) 
so that all may be judged who did not believe the truth, but who consented to iniquity.

(2 Thessalonians 2:13) 
But we ought to give thanks to God always for you, brothers beloved by God, because God chose you as the first fruits for salvation, in the sanctification of the Spirit, and the faith of truth:

(2 Thessalonians 2:14) 
to which He called you through our Gospel, so that you might obtain the glory of our Lord Jesus Christ.

(2 Thessalonians 2:15) 
So then, brothers, stand firm and hold to the traditions that you were taught, either by word of mouth, or by our letter.

(2 Thessalonians 2:16) 
Now may our Lord Jesus Christ Himself, and God and our Father, who loved us, and gave everlasting consolation and good hope through grace,

(2 Thessalonians 2:17) 
exhort your hearts, and confirm them in every good work and word.

(2 Thessalonians 3:1) 
Finally, brothers, pray for us, that the word of the Lord spreads and is glorified, just as it is with you.

(2 Thessalonians 3:2) 
And pray that we might be delivered from unreasonable and evil men. Because not everyone has faith.

(2 Thessalonians 3:3) 
But God is faithful, and He will strengthen you and guard you from evil.

(2 Thessalonians 3:4) 
Moreover, we trust in the Lord concerning you, that you both do the things that we command you, and will do them.

(2 Thessalonians 3:5) 
And may the Lord direct your hearts in the love of God and in the patience of Christ.

(2 Thessalonians 3:6) 
Now we command you, brothers, in the name of our Lord Jesus Christ, that you withdraw from every brother who walks disorderly, and not according to the tradition which they received from us.

(2 Thessalonians 3:7) 
For you yourselves know how it is necessary to imitate us: because we did not act disorderly among you,

(2 Thessalonians 3:8) 
nor did we eat anyone's bread for free, but we worked in labor and toil night and day, so that we would not burden any of you.

(2 Thessalonians 3:9) 
Not because we did not have the authority, but to give ourselves as a model to you, so that you might imitate us.

(2 Thessalonians 3:10) 
For even when we were with you, we were commanding you this: that if anyone does not want to work, neither let him eat.

(2 Thessalonians 3:11) 
For we hear that some of you are walking disorderly, doing no work, but acting as busybodies.

(2 Thessalonians 3:12) 
Now those of that kind we command and exhort in the Lord Jesus Christ, that working quietly, they eat their own bread.

(2 Thessalonians 3:13) 
But you, brothers, do not grow weary in doing good.

(2 Thessalonians 3:14) 
And if anyone does not obey our word through this letter, note this one, and do not associate with him, so that he may be ashamed.

(2 Thessalonians 3:15) 
And do not consider him an enemy, but admonish him as a brother.

(2 Thessalonians 3:16) 
Now may the Lord of peace Himself give you peace always in every place. The Lord be with all of you.

(2 Thessalonians 3:17) 
The greeting by my own hand, Paul, which is the sign in every letter; I write in this way.

(2 Thessalonians 3:18) 
The grace of our Lord Jesus Christ be with all of you. Amen.

(1 Timothy 1:1) 
Paul, an Apostle of Jesus Christ, according to the command of God our Savior, and of Christ Jesus, our hope,

(1 Timothy 1:2) 
To Timothy, a beloved son in the faith. Grace, mercy, and peace from God the Father, and Christ Jesus, our Lord.

(1 Timothy 1:3) 
As I requested you to stay in Ephesus, on my way to Macedonia, so that you would command certain people not to teach differently,

(1 Timothy 1:4) 
nor to give heed to fables and endless genealogies: which give rise to disputes, rather than to the edification of God, which is in faith.

(1 Timothy 1:5) 
Now the goal of the commandment is charity, from a pure heart, and a good conscience, and faith unfeigned.

(1 Timothy 1:6) 
From these things some, having strayed, are turned aside to vain speech,

(1 Timothy 1:7) 
desiring to be teachers of the law, though they understand neither what they say, nor the things concerning which they make affirmation.

(1 Timothy 1:8) 
But we know that the law is good, if one uses it lawfully:

(1 Timothy 1:9) 
knowing this, that the law is not made for the just man, but for the unjust and disobedient, for the impious and for sinners, for the wicked and defiled, for murderers of fathers, and murderers of mothers,

(1 Timothy 1:10) 
fornicators, those who practice homosexuality, kidnappers, liars, perjurers, and if there is anything else that goes against sound doctrine;

(1 Timothy 1:11) 
according to the Gospel of the glory of the blessed God, which was entrusted to me.

(1 Timothy 1:12) 
And I give thanks to him who has strengthened me, even Christ Jesus our Lord, because he has judged me faithful, putting me into the ministry,

(1 Timothy 1:13) 
who was before a blasphemer, and a persecutor, and contumelious. But I obtained mercy, because I did it ignorantly, in unbelief.

(1 Timothy 1:14) 
And the grace of our Lord abounded with faith and the love that is in Christ Jesus.

(1 Timothy 1:15) 
Faithful is the word, and worthy of all acceptance, that Christ Jesus came into the world to save sinners, of whom I am chief.

(1 Timothy 1:16) 
But for this reason I obtained mercy: that in me first Christ Jesus might show forth all patience, for the example of those who would believe in him unto life everlasting.

(1 Timothy 1:17) 
Now to the King of ages, immortal, invisible, the only God, be honor and glory for ever and ever. Amen.

(1 Timothy 1:18) 
This charge I commit to you, Timothy, my son, in accordance with the prophecies previously made about you, that by them you may wage the good warfare,

(1 Timothy 1:19) 
holding faith and a good conscience, which some, having thrust aside, have suffered shipwreck concerning the faith.

(1 Timothy 1:20) 
Among these are Hymenaeus and Alexander, whom I have delivered to Satan, that they may learn not to blaspheme.

(1 Timothy 2:1) 
I ask, then, that, first of all, that there be prayers of supplication, prayers of petition, and thanksgiving offered for all people:

(1 Timothy 2:2) 
Pray for those in authority, and all those who govern, so that we may live a calm and tranquil life, with all piety and chastity.

(1 Timothy 2:3) 
This is good, and acceptable in the sight of God, our Savior,

(1 Timothy 2:4) 
Who wills all people to be saved, and to come to the knowledge of the truth.

(1 Timothy 2:5) 
For there is only one God, and only one mediator between God and humankind, the man Christ Jesus:

(1 Timothy 2:6) 
Who gave Himself as a redemption for all, as a testimony in his own time:

(1 Timothy 2:7) 
I, Paul, have been placed as a herald, and an apostle—I speak the truth and do not lie—a teacher of the Gentiles in faith and truth.

(1 Timothy 2:8) 
I want, therefore, men to pray in every place, lifting up holy hands, without anger or quarreling.

(1 Timothy 2:9) 
Likewise, women should adorn themselves in modest apparel, with decency and moderation, not with braided hair, gold, pearls, or costly clothes,

(1 Timothy 2:10)
